Wangting Township, Robbery Injures People

In the fifth ward, third district, of Nanbang Township in Wangting Township, at about 3:00 AM on the 13th, more than ten robbers arrived, each holding firearms, swarming to the home of villager Qian Dabao. They tied up Qian Dabao and his mother, Qian Xu, and subjected them to beatings. As a result, they robbed gold jewelry and clothing worth more than 200 yuan.

Three Suicide Cases in One Day

Suicide cases have emerged one after another in Suzhou. Yesterday, three suicide cases occurred. They are recorded as follows: (1) Huang Zhou Yingzhen, 34 years old, concubine of Huang Liangsheng, No. 1 Yaoji Lane, Bifengfang, inside the city, committed suicide by drowning in the Zhujiaqiao stream in Guanli Road outside Loumen at noon on the 12th due to discord with the wife. In the afternoon, the district inspection office sent personnel to verify the identity and prepared a coffin for the family. (2) Cui Ruiyuan, a 19-year-old apprentice from Liu Dasheng Tung Oil Shop outside Qimen, committed suicide by swallowing opium in Room 11 of the Lichang Hotel due to the pain of unemployment. The district inspection office also sent personnel to verify the identity and prepared a coffin for burial. (3) Lin Chen, 20 years old, wife of Lin Genlin, who opened a disaster relief noodle shop at No. 6 Hengjie Street, Loumen, committed suicide by drowning in Ermenkou, Loumen, after being beaten by her husband. She was rescued by a police officer and was fortunate to be reborn.

Wuxi, Military Officer Who Embezzled Funds Arrested in Wuxi

Wang Mengting, a supply officer with the rank of major in the Second Regiment of the Jiangxi Nanchang Tax Police, a native of Suzhou, absconded with 850 yuan in salary and two orderlies, Wang Xiaosan, last month. After the regiment commander discovered the incident, he immediately telegraphed the public security bureaus of Beijing and Shanghai to arrest him. After leaving Jiangxi, Wang Mengting took Wang Xiaosan by ship to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, Wang Xiaosan suddenly stole the salary and fled. Wang Mengting was extremely frustrated. After arriving in Shanghai, he heard that Shanghai had received a telegram from Nanchang and knew that it was difficult to gain a foothold. He fled to this county the day before yesterday and stayed at the No. 1 Hotel on Tongyun Road. The public security bureau of this county had also received a telegram requesting the arrest. After learning that Wang was staying at the No. 1 Hotel, they sent detective Wang Shuanglin and others to the address and arrested Wang Mengting and took him to the bureau. Zhang, the section chief of the Third Section, interrogated him in court and ordered him to be temporarily detained to await the arrival of officials to bring him back to justice.

Exhibition of Giant Whale

The Taian Orphanage recently has a large whale, 13 zhang (approximately 43 meters) long, weighing 40 tons, or 67,200 jin (approximately 33,600 kilograms). There is also a foreign conjoined twins. The orphanage is arranging to transport it by special train to Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and display it along the way in Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, Jiaxing, Hangzhou, etc. It will arrive in Wuxi tomorrow (15th) and be on display at the Gongyun Bridge in front of the train station. Admission is one 角 (dime) per person, half price for children. Students who visit in groups can also receive preferential treatment. The ticket sales will be used by the orphanage to raise orphans in North China.

Rural Woman Commits Suicide by Ingesting Opium

Wu Zhongda, 30 years old, a resident of the Wu Zhongda of the Shuiqueli area near Houqiao Town in the Ninth District, opened a brothel in Shanghai. In his youth, he hired Shao Qiaosheng, a tailor from Anzhen, to marry his daughter Gendi. They married in 1929. Gendi lived in the countryside, and Wu took a concubine in Shanghai, neglecting his wife's livelihood. In recent years, Wu has shrunk his brothel and changed it to a hotel, but he was not good at business and suffered huge losses, leading to bankruptcy. Gendi, facing a broken livelihood, suddenly had the idea of suicide and secretly ingested raw opium yesterday afternoon. After being discovered by neighbors, a doctor was called to provide emergency treatment, but it was too late. She died in the evening. Shao Qiaosheng, the woman's father, heard the news and launched a major protest, intending to report to the local branch to request an autopsy.

Nantong, Gang of Bandits Defeated on Nantong Coast

On the coast of Jiangbei's Nantong, a large gang of Haizhou bandits invaded, and the situation was extremely rampant. The Provincial Security Department telegraphed Shen Yishan, the captain of the maritime guerrilla team, ordering him to lead his troops to suppress them. Shen's troops set out from Fengjue and sunk two bandit ships. The remaining bandits fled north.

Jingjiang, Large Quantity of Opium Confiscated in Xialiuwei

At 2:30 PM yesterday, the Taikoo Company's Huangpu ship arrived near Xialiuwei Port in the Seventh District and threw two bags of opium, weighing 66 and a half catties (approximately 40 kilograms). A water patrol boat from the Public Security Bureau was protecting it nearby. Just as they were about to retrieve it, a patrol boat from the Provincial Maritime Public Security Third Detachment, stationed in Bajiwei Port, arrived to investigate. A conflict broke out, and gunfire was exchanged. The opium traffickers Tian Juquan (aka Tian Jingan), Liu Yu (aka Liu Xueyi, chief of the Public Security Bureau patrol), Zhang Heqing (aka Zhang Zhilian, patrol officer of the Public Security Bureau), and a No. 2 box gun (number 2111) and two bags of opium were seized by the water police. The two sides were in a stalemate. Chen Xingya, the patrol officer of the county water patrol team, immediately sent a police officer to report to the General Bureau. Director Zhang led twelve armed police officers to the scene at 3:00 AM that night, and the personnel and contraband were placed under custody at the Seventh District Office. All the officials of the district office mediated for an entire night before a resolution was reached. 49 and a half catties of opium and Tian Juquan were handed over to the county government. The rest was ignored. The county government was unaware of the details and detained Tian Juquan and confiscated the opium.

Haimen, Fierce Battle Between Police and Bandits in Tianbu Township

Zhou Zengchuan, the captain of the First Battalion of the Guard Regiment, and Jing Bo, the chief of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau, jointly led twenty members of the regiment and police on patrol at the border between the First and Second Districts at 2:00 AM yesterday (11th). When they arrived west of the Wu Shaoshi store in Tianbu Township in the Second District, more than ten robbers suddenly came face to face. The regiment and police shouted for them to stop, and the robbers immediately opened fire. The regiment and police returned fire. For a moment, the sound of gunfire was as dense as a string of firecrackers, and bullets fell like rain. Before long, the robbers suddenly shouted "not good" and fled southeast in droves. The night was still dark, and reeds grew densely along the road, so the regiment and police did not dare to pursue them, fearing an ambush. When they advanced to the original location of the robbers, they saw two bandits dead after being shot. Villagers identified them as Shi Zhiqiu and Huang Yunxian, both living in Jiusi Township in the First District. A box gun with eleven bullets and a large flashlight were found on Shi's body. Ten handgun bullets and a洋燭 (wax candle) were found in Huang's pocket. They continued to search the homes of Shi and Huang, but their families had fled. Thirty-six box gun bullets and 13 pieces of clothing and bedding and a wallet were found separately. Yuan Wenhuan, Zhang Guanchou, Ni Baoxiang, and three other suspects were arrested near Dalian Township in the First District. They were all presented to the county government for interrogation in the afternoon.

Gaoyou, Patrol Team Intercepts Flesh Ransom

Yang Jiang's barge was sailing from Zhongyou to Jiangjiaba the day before yesterday. Unexpectedly, when it reached the reeds at the river mouth, it suddenly encountered six bandits who fired their guns as a warning and shouted for the barge to stop. They swarmed onto the boat and searched, stealing a handbag containing 60 yuan in silver and clothing. They also kidnapped Yang Jiang's granddaughter-in-law, Ms. Liu, and her eight-month-old great-grandson. At that time, Hu Xiaojin, the patrol officer of the Second Detachment of the Gaobao Patrol Team, was leading a team patrolling the lake. Suddenly hearing the sound of gunfire, they immediately pursued them, knocking down one of the kidnapped Ms. Liu, a flesh ransom. The bandits had already disappeared. As it was getting late, it was not convenient to pursue them further. However, Yang Jiang's great-grandson was still in danger. Team Leader Wang of the Gaobao Patrol Team has ordered detectives to investigate in all directions.

Jiashan, Widow Commits Suicide to Preserve Chastity and Follow Husband

In the area of Xu Jia Bang north of Dingjiazhai, the farmer Xu Zhongyou had two sons, Erguan and Fusheng. Erguan married a woman the year before last, but died of illness. Fusheng married a Ms. Li. Ms. Li had some knowledge of writing and was named Yueying. After marriage, their relationship became very close. Unexpectedly, Fusheng's tuberculosis became severe and he soon passed away. Ms. Li was extremely saddened and vowed to preserve her chastity. The day before yesterday, her brother-in-law Erguan actually wanted to marry his brother's widow and had obtained the consent of his parents. When Ms. Li heard about it, she secretly hanged herself last night to follow her husband in death. It was truly tragic.

The Bride is Actually the Goddess of Fire

Xu Kefu, a resident of Hujia Bang in Yangmiao Town, married his son Zhuoying the day before yesterday. Xu was a wealthy man, and the bride, Zhou Meizhen, had received an education. Therefore, guests gathered and the wedding was extremely extravagant. The bride's trousseau was also quite rich. Unexpectedly, on the evening of the same day, just as the newlyweds were holding their wedding ceremony, a fire suddenly broke out in the kitchen. For a moment, the flames soared and could not be approached. Relatives and friends fled for their lives, in a state of extreme embarrassment, with loud cries and shouts, and the order was chaotic. Fortunately, someone managed to escort the bride back to her parents' home. All the houses, buildings, and utensils were reduced to ashes. In the chaos, the groom broke a leg and was taken to Jiashan Hospital for treatment that night.

Hangzhou, Hanghui Highway Automobile Robbed

Since the opening of the Hanghui Highway last year, travelers and merchants from Zhejiang and Anhui provinces have found it convenient. At 10:00 AM on the 10th of this month, a Huizhou man, Cheng, and two tea merchants, Fang and others, took a small charter car, Anhui character 1032, from She County to Hangzhou. At 3:15 PM, when they drove through the area where Moshikeng in Lin'an County in Zhejiang Province meets Zhoushan Station, two robbers suddenly appeared, each holding a handgun, and shouted for them to stop. Cheng was robbed of 65 yuan in paper money. Fang and others were robbed of a gold ring worth one钱 (approximately 3.7 grams) each and 6 yuan in silver. They then left. Fortunately, more than 2,000 yuan in paper money was hidden in a handbag and was not searched and robbed. The incident was reported to the Lin'an County government by telephone, requesting the arrest of the robbers.

Hefei, Adultery Murder Case Occurs in Liu Mu Alley

Li Decai, a native of Liu'an, who lived in Liu Mu Alley in the north gate, was acquainted with a woman from Changzhou, Ms. Li, and lived in Hefei. Currently, Li Decai is addicted to opium and is in dire straits. Ms. Li then had an affair with Li Jingnan, a clerk at the Hu Hongsheng Paper Shop on Dongmen Street. On the night of the 9th, when Li Jingnan was having a secret rendezvous with Ms. Li, Li Decai found out. Burning with anger, he charged into the bedroom with a kitchen knife and hacked at the adulterous couple. Li Jingnan's head, neck, and arms were cut six or seven times, and Ms. Li's abdomen, legs, and lower body were cut four or five times. They both cried for help, alarming the landlord, Wu Qifa, who opened the door to look. Li Decai then abandoned the knife and fled. Li Jingnan and Ms. Li were both lying in a pool of blood, on the verge of death. On the morning of the 10th, the Wu family reported the case to the military police and the court, causing a sensation throughout the city. The crowd of onlookers was huge. A serious manhunt is underway.

Chu Family Robbed of Large Amount of Gold Jewelry

The home of Chu Wuluan, a wealthy man in the upper part of Youfang Lane, had purchased a large amount of gold jewelry and gold bars during the life of his father, Chu Huaiqing, and stored it under the floor in his mother, Zhang's room. Even the family members did not know about it. Unexpectedly, last night, seven or eight robbers climbed over the back wall and hid in the kitchen. When Chu's daughter-in-law, who was in confinement, ordered the maid to prepare supper, she suddenly saw the robbers with their faces covered and was greatly frightened and wanted to run away. The robbers stopped the woman and then pushed into Chu's mother's bedroom. Chu's mother knew they were being robbed and hurriedly took out 400 yuan to give to them. They ignored it and went straight to the head of the bed, moved the jar of salted eggs, pried open the floor, and took out two large boxes containing more than 120 taels of pure gold and more than 20 gold bars. Together with the 400 yuan given by Chu's mother, they were all robbed. Afterwards, the military police were reported to arrest the robbers, but they had disappeared without a trace. However, since the Chu family had buried the gold more than ten years ago, only two groups of people knew about it, so there was no suspicion. Also, since the neighbors were very suspicious, it was reported today and more than twenty people were arrested for strict questioning.

Local News

Zhang Gongquan Discusses His Impressions of Traveling in Sichuan

Zhang Gongquan, the general manager of the Bank of China, had many impressions from this trip to Sichuan. Therefore, he wrote an article on his findings for the reference of all circles to develop Sichuan Province. The record is as follows:

Trade Deficit Exhausts Finances

This time, I traveled to Sichuan, first to Chongqing, then to Neijiang, Zigong, and then to Chengdu. From Chengdu to Jiading, Xufu, Luzhou, and back to Chongqing, and then to Beipei, traveling for 45 days. Sichuan naturally has all the common problems of various provinces, such as poor politics, excessive tax burdens, difficult lives for farmers, reduced purchasing power, trade imbalances, and exhausted finances.

There are Four Special Diseases

The first is the defense zone system. Before last year, Sichuan was almost divided into four or five countries, with defense zones for the 21st Army, the 24th Army, the 28th Army, and the 29th Army, each seemingly independent. Even taxes and currencies were managed independently. When goods were transferred through a defense zone, they had to be taxed once. Since the end of the Second Liu War, Liu Wenhui has retreated to Xikang, and the defense zone run by Liu Xiang has greatly expanded. His power has exceeded that of other armies. The power of other armies, such as Yang, Deng, and Tian, is far less than before, but the defense zone system still exists. The second is the heavy collection of land taxes. Due to financial difficulties, each defense zone can collect land taxes more than ten times a year, averaging at least seven times, and the people have to work hard to bear the burden. Their suffering can be imagined. The third is miscellaneous taxes. Various provinces have abolished Likin, but Sichuan Province taxes various goods passing through, almost every item has a tax, and the establishment of checkpoints for collection is no different from Likin in disguise. The fourth is the non-unification of currency. The provinces now use silver dollars, but Sichuan has a special Sichuan silver dollar, which is of a lower standard than the silver dollar, about 100 yuan lower per 1,000 yuan. There are also other areas that use small silver dollars.

Abundant Natural Resources and New Thoughts

The population of Sichuan is almost the highest among the provinces, said to be 70 million, more than the entire country of Japan, and its reproductive capacity is still increasing daily. Farmers are exceptionally hardworking. The fields we have traveled through have almost no wasteland. The fields are neat and tidy. It is known at a glance that they are a hard-working people. Secondly, natural resources are abundant, and the land is fertile. The entire province produces almost everything except cotton. It can be said that where there are people, there is land, and where there is land, there is wealth. Sichuan is enough to be called it. It is a pity that the wealth is used to raise soldiers and fight civil wars, which is a disservice to the people who work hard all year round and the natural treasures. At the same time, one thing to note is that the people of Sichuan have new ideas and are good at chasing trends. Now Chongqing has a public treasury and a securities exchange. Generally, things from Shanghai are easily imported. This is also a great convenience for the future reform of Sichuan. There is no shortage of ambitious people in society, such as Mr. Lu Zuofu, who is painstakingly engaged in social work and striving for spiritual construction, all of which are noteworthy and gratifying.

The Hope for Awareness from All Armies in the Future

Currently, Liu Xiang, the Supervisor-General, is diligently engaged in bandit suppression. He has expressed that after the bandit suppression is completed, he will immediately engage in post-disaster recovery, find ways to reduce the army, reorganize internally, and then engage in construction. His enthusiasm for protecting Sichuan and his determination to reorganize Sichuan, as well as his personal integrity, are truly admirable. However, the most important thing is still the awareness of each army, jointly abolishing the defense zone system, unifying politics and finance, reducing the burden on the people, and having a reasonable tax system, so that the people can have a little respite, indirectly prevent the people from becoming communists, and directly promote the increase of production. Only then can we talk about post-disaster recovery and hope for the success of the red suppression. Otherwise, I am afraid that the cart will be put before the horse. It is especially hoped that the military and political authorities who have never left Sichuan in the past will travel to other provinces more, so that the provinces and Nanjing and Shanghai can communicate more with Sichuan, then the progress and construction of Sichuan will be more rapid.

Shanghai Merchants Should Have Vision for Sichuan

Given the large population and abundant resources of Sichuan, and its area almost equal to that of Germany, Sichuan Province should be regarded as a large market for Shanghai's industries. Needless to say, in terms of consumption, even for cotton yarn alone, if Sichuan Province can be stable and the people's purchasing power slightly increased, then the cotton yarn produced by Shanghai's Chinese yarn factories can easily be absorbed by Sichuan Province alone. However, if we want to make Sichuan a sales market for Shanghai's manufactured goods, we must find ways to increase the purchasing power of the people of Sichuan. To increase purchasing power, we must increase the productivity of the people of Sichuan. To increase production, we must also help Sichuan sell its products, so that Sichuan's exports and imports can offset each other. Therefore, on the one hand, there should be more technical personnel going to Sichuan to help plan various constructions, and on the other hand, when the political situation is slightly stable and the currency system is slightly reorganized, funds should be gradually input to increase its production funds. This is the vision that Shanghai's industrial circles should have. In short, people from other provinces should approach the people of Sichuan with deep sympathy to fulfill their responsibility of guidance.

Developing Greater Shanghai: The Municipal Government Issues Public Bonds Totaling 3.5 Million Yuan Approved by the Central Political Conference

According to the Central News Agency, this city is a major port in East Asia, with ships gathering and talents flourishing. It is not only the economic and cultural center of the country, but also related to international observation. The planning and improvement of municipal administration should not be delayed. Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of this city, is actively seeking the development of new urban areas in order to adapt to future needs and construction convenience. Since the completion and relocation of the new building of the municipal government in the city center, the citizens' perceptions have been refreshed. However, the construction of undertakings is in full swing, and local resources are limited. According to the city's original income, it is feared that it will not be enough to cover the application of the original undertaking. Moreover, great construction is not possible. Therefore, Mayor Wu requested the Central Government to approve the issuance of 3.5 million yuan of 7% public bonds in this city in the 23rd year of the Republic, using the donations and taxes of this city as collateral. It has been resolved and approved by the Central Political Conference, and it can be issued after being reviewed and approved by the Legislative Yuan. It is reported that the use of the public bonds has been stipulated as follows:

Building a Sports Field

This city is the education center of the country. The promotion of sports is especially valued by the central government. Moreover, the next National Games has been scheduled to be held in this city next year, and the Far East Games will also be held in Shanghai. Therefore, this city urgently needs to build a large public sports field to meet the needs of the environment.

Establishing a Museum

Modern science is prosperous, and the organization of national heritage is closely related to the promotion of new culture. The importance of this city's position, for the research institution of museums, is still lacking. Since the establishment of a public museum, to promote impressions, and the ancient relics of the Forbidden City, a part of the belonging, are now rented for storage. If the hospital is built, it can also be deposited and kept in moderation, so as to avoid the need to find another storage money, resulting in more difficulties.

Establishing a Library

This city is also a gathering place of talents. The Oriental Library, established by the Commercial Press, did exist before, but it was destroyed by Japanese artillery fire during the "January 28th" Incident and has not been restored. At present, the public and private libraries are all poorly equipped. At the moment of advocating academic national salvation, this city urgently needs to build a larger public library to seek the revival of culture.

Building a Municipal Hospital

This city has the most dense population among major cities, and should have perfect facilities for public health. Therefore, the municipal government is now planning to allocate a part of the public bonds to build a perfect municipal hospital, so that all citizens can enjoy the convenience and safety of medicine.

Organizing Slaughterhouses

This city is the largest commercial port in Asia. Even the slaughter of animals has long been improved in the concession, and the concession authorities have set up slaughterhouses for application. However, there are no such facilities in the Chinese boundary, which is closely related to the public health of the citizens. Although the municipal government has discussed the organization, it has not been realized due to limited financial resources. Therefore, this matter will be organized after the issuance of public bonds this time.

Repairing Various Roads

Since the January 28th Incident, the disaster area in Zhabei has been vast. Although public bonds for post-war reconstruction have been raised to provide relief, only a part of the work can be completed. The most urgent things to be reorganized and expanded at present are (A) the construction and repair of various roads and bridges in the Balian Special Zone, (B) the construction of ditches, (C) the completion of Zhongshan Road, and (D) the construction and improvement of water and electricity roads. These are all of great significance to the development of the city center. Therefore, work can be started as soon as the public bonds are sold.

Japanese Ambassador Arima Reported to Japan That Kuramoto Was Found. The Japanese Embassy Received a Notice from Beijing at 4 PM Yesterday.

According to the Central News Agency, the disappearance of Kuramoto Hideaki, the Japanese Deputy Consul in Beijing, on the night of the 8th, has attracted the attention of Chinese and foreign people. After Wang Jingwei, the President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Foreign Affairs, learned of the news, he immediately ordered the military and police of the capital to mobilize and search. The Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai and Hankou also received orders to sail to the waters of Xiaguan one after another, which aroused the attention of Chinese and foreign people. It is now learned that Deputy Consul Kuramoto was found by our side at Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum in the capital at about 1:00 pm yesterday and sent to the Capital Police Department. After receiving the report, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs immediately notified Suma, the Japanese Consul General in Nanjing, in writing. Suma reported to Ambassador Arima by long-distance telephone between Beijing and Shanghai at about 4:00 pm. The news obtained in this port is recorded as follows:

Our Side Worked Hard to Search

After Deputy Consul Kuramoto disappeared in Beijing on the night of the 8th, the Capital Police Department and the Garrison Headquarters immediately received orders to search in all directions, day and night. Shimizu, the police chief of the Japanese Embassy, also sent personnel to assist in the search, but there were no results for many days. The Japanese warships stationed on the Shanghai River and the Japanese warships stationed in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River were also ordered to sail to Beijing one after another and stationed in the waters of Xiaguan. At the same time, the Japanese expatriates in the capital believed that Kuramoto's disappearance in the capital was obviously due to our country's lack of protection, and they were quite indignant. As a result, the Kuramoto disappearance incident has become increasingly serious in recent days.

Found Near Ming Mausoleum

It was not until about 1:00 pm yesterday that Deputy Consul Kuramoto was safely found at Ming Mausoleum. According to the Japanese news in this port, at about 1:00 pm yesterday, the Ming Mausoleum guard accidentally found a Japanese person nearby. At that time, he did not know that he was Deputy Consul Kuramoto, who had been searched for for several days but could not be found. He reported to the Capital Police Department. After receiving the report, the Police Department immediately sent two armed policemen and one plainclothes detective to go to the place of discovery to confirm the truth and hired a car to send him to the Police Department. After learning of the news, the Japanese side also sent personnel to Ming Mausoleum to find and identify him. At that time, Deputy Consul Kuramoto had already been sent to the Police Department.

Shanghai Japanese Consulate News

According to Iwai Eiichi, the representative of the Information Office of the Japanese Consulate General in this port, told the Central News Agency reporter that the Shanghai Consulate General had received a report that Deputy Consul Kuramoto was found in Beijing. The details of the discovery are unknown. Iwai also said that Suma, the Consul General of Japan in Nanjing, reported to Ambassador Arima by long-distance telephone between Beijing and Shanghai after 4:00 pm, saying, "The Consulate General of Japan in Nanjing has just received a formal notification from the Chinese Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating that Deputy Consul Kuramoto was found this afternoon (that is, yesterday)." The wording is very simple, so detailed information cannot be disclosed, and so on.

Arima Reported to Japan by Telegram

After receiving the report, Ambassador Arima immediately telegraphed to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Tokyo to report. It is also learned that the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai had not received a detailed report on the discovery of Kuramoto until 5:00 pm, so the office hours were extended yesterday to wait for the telegram.

Central Bank Invests in the Construction of National Grain Warehouses. The Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau of Eight Provinces Will Be Run by the Central Government. Grain Warehouses Will Be Built First in Eight Places Including Shanghai and Kaifeng.

According to the Shanghai Times News Agency, the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau, which was produced by the Eight Provinces Grain Conference, was originally vigorously promoted by Chairman Jiang. The share capital was 2 million yuan, of which 1 million yuan was allocated separately by the provinces, and the central government was responsible for borrowing 1 million yuan. Unfortunately, the provinces should pay the salary, which is of no help. Therefore, Gu Shengxin, the director of the preparation of the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau, and Wu Huanru, the deputy director, found it difficult to advance or retreat. They went to Gan the other day to ask for instructions and clarified all the difficulties. However, Jiang still insisted on active progress. If the provinces no longer pay the money, they decided to return all the money that has been paid as it is, and the central government will completely fund the operation. At that time, Kong Xiangxi happened to be in Gan, and Jiang personally instructed and ordered Cai Kong to plan and the Central Bank to fund the progress.

Gu Xinyi Visited Cai Kong for Days

This time, Kong Xiangxi, the president of the Central Bank, came to Shanghai after the financial meeting. Since the Grain Transportation Bureau had been instructed by Jiang, it must be implemented according to the order. Gu Xinyi was repeatedly invited to discuss the progress plan, and Gu reported all the preparations of the Grain Transportation Bureau and the amount of money paid by the provinces and cities. Kong believed that the organization of the Grain Transportation Bureau was originally handled by merchants with their own funds. Now that the merchant shares cannot be paid in full, if the central government takes charge, the organization must be changed, and it must be discussed with Song Ziwen of the National Economic Commission. In the future, this agency may have to be subordinate to the National Economic Commission and merged into the Grain Control Association that is being organized and established. Therefore, he promised to study all the rules and regulations within a few days and then discuss them with Song before deciding on a concrete plan.

Invest in the Construction of National Warehouses

The Shanghai Times News Agency reporter learned from the Central Bank yesterday that Kong is now willing to actively plan the progress of the Grain Transportation Bureau. However, the most important thing is the construction of grain warehouses, because the most important function of the Transportation and Sales Bureau is to regulate grain. In other words, the state's power is used to control the market price of grain. When farmers have surplus grain, the Transportation and Sales Bureau will purchase it in large quantities and store it for a long time. When farmers lack grain, they will take it out of the warehouse and supply it in large quantities. This is the general hub for regulating supply and demand. Without large grain warehouses in various places, it will not be enough to cope with it. Now Kong has decided to build a large-scale new-style warehouse in each of the eight places including Shanghai, Nanjing, Wuhu, Jiujiang, Hankou, Changsha, Kaifeng, and Luoyang. At least 3 million yuan of grain can be stored to prepare for emergencies. The required funds are about 500,000 yuan for each place, totaling 4 million yuan, which will be invested and constructed by the Central Bank. The Shanghai Municipal Government originally planned to carry out the construction of these warehouses and had detailed budgets and construction plans for Class A, B, C, and D. Later, the progress was suspended due to the difficulty of raising funds. Now President Kong has instructed the municipal government authorities to submit this construction plan for reference.

China Aviation Corporation Discussed: The Shanghai-Ping Route Detours to Weihai. Weihai Has a Large Existing Airfield. Takeoffs and Landings Are Handled by the Management Office on Behalf of the Company.

The China Aviation Corporation previously received a letter from Xu Dongfan, the Weihaiwei Management Commissioner, stating that Weihaiwei is an important port in North China. In addition to the highway between Yantai and Weihai for automobiles, the land transportation is quite far from the Jiaoji and Jinpu railways, so passengers and mail traveling by land are quite inconvenient. More than three years have passed since the port was recovered. At present, all local administrative affairs have been actively carried out, and it will surely become an important commercial port in North China and the only military port in Beiyang. Land transportation must rely on aviation. The Changfeng area of Weihaiwei has a huge airfield, and the necessary equipment for aircraft takeoffs and landings has been completed. If the airline adds Weihai to the route and makes it a takeoff and landing station, passengers and mail traveling to and from Weihai will be greatly facilitated, and the company will be spared the work and expenses of opening a field and other equipment, which can also achieve twice the result with half the effort. After receiving the letter, the airline attached great importance to it and immediately replied, stating that if the Shanghai-Ping route detours to Weihai, it will have to be increased from eight hours to ten hours. It is currently under discussion. Later, Commissioner Xu telegraphed again, stating that flying and landing during the day would take 11 hours. During the spring, summer, and autumn seasons, it should be within a possible range and should not cause difficulties. However, the matter concerns aviation time, and the company should directly measure and allocate the time and re-specify it, or it may be shortened. However, after setting up a station, the Weihai Management Office can assign personnel to handle the care of aircraft takeoffs and landings, as well as the reception of passengers and the sale and collection of tickets, purely as an obligation, so that the company can be exempted from the station expenses. The company is now conducting in-depth research on this issue.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau: Reorganizing the Machine Style and Expanding the Lines. The Number of Lines to the Concession Has Increased to 70 Pairs.

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications requested the Ministry of Communications to reorganize the user small exchange and expand the wiring business in order to maintain the telephone service. The details are recorded as follows:

Reorganizing the Machine Style

The telephone bureau believes that the small exchanges of users in various districts have different styles, which makes it difficult to maintain. Therefore, it intends to determine the reorganization method and submit it to the Ministry of Communications for approval. According to the number of relay lines and extensions required by users, it is divided into three types: intercom type, button type, and floor-standing type. Those who use one to sixteen extensions will be equipped with intercom type exchanges. Ten to sixteen extensions can be equipped with button type exchanges. Those who use sixteen to fifty extensions will use floor-standing type exchanges. It has already been ordered from various electrical material firms to purchase products manufactured in China. Once they are delivered, they will be reorganized one after another.

Expanding the Number of Lines

There were 50 pairs of existing lines to connect to the concession. Recently, the number of users requesting installation has increased, and the telephone business has also developed accordingly. In addition, after the bureau canceled the five-point call fee, the original number of pairs of lines was insufficient for application. Therefore, the telephone bureau plans to expand the number of Chinese-concession call lines from 50 pairs to 70 pairs in the near future, and then expand again in the future according to business needs. The zero-number switchboard connecting to the concession will also be expanded in response to user needs. In addition, after the telephones in Longhua, Pudong, and other places were reformed, the telephone bureau specially compiled a new directory for the 23rd year. The bureau sent a letter to each user with a coupon to receive it, which can be started in about 20 days.

Subsidizing Chinese Silk Exports: Chinese and Foreign Merchant Ships Reduce Freight Rates. Domestic Silk Cocoons Reduce by Half Price. Silk Shipped to the United States Is Charged Two Yuan per Piece.

In order to rescue Chinese silk exports, in addition to the ten items on reforming the silk and silkworm method, which were announced to Shanghai by the Ministry of Industry long ago, there are reductions in the transportation costs of silk cocoons and various donations and taxes. The Executive Yuan has transferred the order to the transportation and finance ministries, and ordered the relevant agencies under their jurisdiction to handle the matter. The Chinese and foreign shipping companies in this port have also received the order and have already drawn up plans to reduce water feet to promote the export of Chinese silk. The situation heard is described as follows:

Domestic Half-Price Charge

After receiving the instructions from the Ministry of Communications, the shipping companies in this port first negotiated the reduction of freight rates for silk cocoons, mulberry seedlings, and other items to rescue silk and silkworms. The state-owned China Merchants Bureau in this port first decided that where the bureau's ships pass, such as when silk cocoons and mulberry seedlings are reported for loading, special reduced rates will be allowed. It was decided that the freight rates set for each route will be charged at half price to show preferential treatment. The bureau has submitted a report to the Ministry of Communications and transferred it to the Ministry of Industry. As for other private shipping companies and railway lines, they are also planning to reduce and charge the transportation rates of silk cocoons and other items.

Foreign Ships Reduce Prices for Transportation and Loading

The most common export goods from Shanghai to the United States via Pacific mail ships between China and the United States are Chinese silk. In the past, shipping companies competed fiercely to load Huzhou silk. From Shanghai to various ports in the United States, such as San Francisco, Seattle, or Vancouver in Canada, each piece of Huzhou silk, weighing 112 pounds, used to cost 12 US dollars. Later, due to mutual competition for loading, the price fell to 6.75 US dollars. Recently, due to the declining export volume, shipping companies continued to call for price cuts, reducing each piece to 5 US dollars, then falling to 4 US dollars, and finally to 3 yuan. It can be said that there is no more cheapest price. Recently, the Chinese government specially requested foreign merchant shippers to reduce the fees to help export Chinese silk, so the Shanghai Pacific Water Foot Association specially convened representatives of various shipping companies to discuss the matter. As a result, starting from the 11th of this month, the price of Chinese silk shipped from Shanghai to the United States will be reduced by another one yuan per piece, and only two US dollars will be charged. Yesterday, all mail ships were notified to implement it uniformly. According to people in the shipping company, the current water feet are only enough to pay the wages for loading, unloading, and storage. The shipping company has no freight feet to get.

Plan to Dredge the Wusong River

Funding: 2.4 Million

Project: Completed within Six Years

Regarding the dredging of the Wusong River, the Ministry of Interior convened representatives from four agencies, including the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Ministry of Communications Waterway Consolidation Committee, and the Shanghai Municipal Government, to hold a meeting in Beijing a few days ago to discuss the dredging plan and funding in detail, and decided to continue to hold a meeting in Beijing yesterday to discuss. As for the dredging funding, it has been predetermined to be 2.4 million yuan, which will be borrowed from the National Economic Commission. Moreover, due to the large area of the river, the dredging work will divide the mouth into four sections, and the entire project is expected to be completed within six years. As for the detailed plan, it is still under discussion.

Families of Jilin Volunteer Army; Central Government Approves Funds for Repatriation to Xinjiang; Four-Article Plan Drafted for Sending Them Back; To Be Handled by Li Du

The families of various units of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, after being forced to retreat into Russia, entered the mainland last spring, residing in Shanghai, Beiping, Tianjin, and other places. It has now been over a year. The livelihoods of these families have been maintained by charitable organizations and various sources of assistance. However, some have been repatriated to their hometowns, while many remain. Among these families, those belonging to Generals Li Du and Commander-in-Chief Wang Delin are the most numerous. Sacrificing for the country and drifting from place to place is not a long-term solution. General Li Du recently submitted a request to the central government for funds to repatriate them to their hometowns, allowing them to seek their own livelihoods. It is reported that the central government has approved the request and has drafted four articles for sending the families of Jilin soldiers to Xinjiang, to be handled by General Li Du. The Far East News Agency reporter has gathered the following information: (1) Repatriation Preparations: (A) Regarding the families of current Jilin military officers residing in Shanghai, Beiping, and Tianjin, Commander Li Du should first conduct a separate investigation, inquire whether they are willing to go to Xinjiang, and record the current position and location of their family heads. A clear list should then be submitted. (B) After the investigation is completed, Commander Li Du should appoint escorts and propose a schedule for gathering the families in Shanghai, Tianjin, and Beiping. The departure time should be determined in consultation with the Ministry of Military Affairs, and the families should be notified to board the train on time. (C) All families willing to go to Xinjiang should be notified to prepare themselves in advance for departure. (2) Repatriation Route: It has been decided that the families will enter Xinjiang via Suining. The transportation will be divided into three stages as follows: (A) From Shanghai via Tianjin and Beiping to Baotou is the first stage. The Railway Department should be instructed to prepare trains for transportation. (B) From Baotou to Ningxia is the second stage. The Suiyuan Provincial Government will provide transportation by automobile. (C) From Ningxia to Dihua is the third stage. The Ningxia Provincial Government will continue the transportation by automobile. (3) Repatriation Funds: A detailed budget should be prepared for the funds. The following temporary advance payment methods are proposed: (A) Subsistence Allowance: Each family member will receive a subsistence allowance of four yuan per day from the date of boarding. The allowance for the first stage will be budgeted by Commander Li Du, issued to the escorts, and accounted for upon completion. The Suiyuan and Ningxia Provincial Governments will verify the number of family members and estimate the transportation time for the second and third stages to calculate and advance the payment. (B) Automobile Expenses: The automobile expenses for the second and third stages will be paid by the Suiyuan and Ningxia Provincial Governments, and a report will be submitted afterward along with the subsistence allowance for verification and reimbursement. (C) The aforementioned expenses will be issued by the Ministry of Finance, and a detailed budget will be prepared for special disbursement. (4) Others: (A) When the families begin their journey, the Xinjiang Provincial Government should be notified by telegram so that each family head can prepare for resettlement. (B) During the journey from Baotou via Ningxia to Dihua, the Ministry of Military Affairs should instruct the garrisons along the way to provide adequate protection from the start of the repatriation.

Such a method is extremely unwise. Qia Da Lumber Company Declares Liquidation Yesterday; Inventory Piling Up, Financial Turnover Impossible; Debts Reach Around 400,000

Qia Da Lumber Company, located at the intersection of Guangfu Road and Meiyuan Road in Zhabei, Shanghai, was established in 1912 and has been in business for over twenty years. Its internal scale is grand, making it a giant in the lumber industry in Shanghai. Manager Zhang Shenju is capable and talented, with an excellent reputation for integrity. Various banks competed to invest in the company. Recently, due to the accumulation of old inventory and sluggish cash flow, coupled with the misunderstanding of creditors, it was unable to maintain operations and declared bankruptcy yesterday.

Investors Affected: When the company was established in 1912, its capital was only twenty to thirty thousand yuan. Due to effective management, its business grew rapidly. During its peak period, its total annual turnover reached seven to eight hundred thousand yuan, and usually it was around four to five hundred thousand yuan. Therefore, it enjoyed a high reputation in the business community. Large and small banks in Shanghai competed to invest in the company, with some investing one to two hundred thousand yuan and others several thousand yuan. This sudden bankruptcy has greatly affected the banking community. It is said that the total amount of debt reaches around 400,000 yuan.

Declaration of Liquidation: After the company's bankruptcy, it immediately entrusted lawyer Tang Wushi and accountant Wang Sifang to handle the liquidation. In addition to sending people to seal up the old inventory and notifying creditors and debtors to register within a specified period, a meeting of creditors will be convened to discuss a proper solution.

What the outside world is saying is clearly untrue.

Ministry of Communications Promulgates Navigation Route Marking Regulations

The Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications yesterday received an order from the Ministry of Communications promulgating the "Navigation Route Marking Regulations" in eight articles, which should be noted by ship merchants sailing along the coast and various rivers across the country. The original text is recorded below: 1. The government shall install various navigation route markers for the safety of ship navigation. 2. The aforementioned markers shall include lighthouses, lightships, buoys, beacons, and fog signals. 3. The construction, repair, supervision, and management of navigation route markers shall be managed by the Ministry of Communications. 4. Local governments may, with the approval of the Ministry of Communications, install necessary navigation route markers. Legal entities may also install them after submitting a request through the local government and obtaining approval from the Ministry of Communications. 5. If the Ministry of Communications deems the navigation route markers in the preceding article to be inappropriate, dangerous, or unnecessary, it may order their modification or removal. If the Ministry of Communications deems it necessary to directly manage the navigation route markers in the preceding article, it may purchase them at a reasonable price. 6. Any of the following acts shall be punishable by a fine of up to 300 yuan: (1) Transferring or obscuring a navigation route marker. (2) Changing the nature of a navigation route marker. (3) Using lights or warning signals in a prohibited area that may confuse the navigation route. 7. Any of the following acts shall be punishable by a fine of up to ten yuan: (1) Colliding with a navigation route marker. (2) Tying a boat or raft to a navigation route marker. (3) Climbing a navigation route marker. (4) Vandalizing a navigation route marker. 8. The implementing regulations of these regulations shall be determined by the Ministry of Communications. 9. These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Young Shao Weizu Despairs of Life; Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Sea from the Wanxiang Ship; Leaves Behind Three Poems Filled with Emotion; Captain Reports to the Shipping Bureau for Record

The Sanbei Shipping Company's Wanxiang ship, which departed from Shanghai to Fujian on the 3rd of this month, suddenly had a young passenger commit suicide by jumping into the sea. He left behind three poems expressing his despair, filled with emotion. The next morning, a tea server discovered the poems and reported them to the ship's captain, Yang Baokang. Mr. Yang immediately reported the incident to the Fujian-Shanghai Shipping Administration authorities, requesting that it be filed for record and investigated. The report is recorded below: "Report Regarding the Discovery of a Missing Passenger"

Missing Passenger Suspected Suicide

We respectfully submit this report regarding the discovery of a missing passenger, suspected to be a suicide, requesting your kind review and filing for record. Our ship departed from Shanghai to Fujian on June 3rd. One third-class passenger, approximately 24 or 25 years old, left his bunk at around 12:00 AM that night, presumably to use the toilet. Therefore, no one suspected anything amiss. However, by the next morning, he had not returned to his bunk. The tea server and nearby passengers noticed and reported to the purser, who reported it to the captain. The captain immediately ordered a ship-wide search, but no trace of him was found. His belongings were then carefully inspected, including a leather suitcase, a felt hat, a business card identifying the man as Shao Weizu of Baoshan, Jiangsu, and a portrait of a man with Western hair (a photograph of which the area was measured at 3.5 cm at the widest point and 4.5 cm at the longest point), and

Three Pessimistic Poems

The first, "What does it matter whether I stay or go, a man's ambition soars; like a grain of rice, I drift across the vast seas." The second, "The future stretches like a long night; past events are like fleeting waves." The third, "Since I was not born at the right time, why begrudge death? A moment can be seen as a hundred years." Reading them filled us with sadness and remorse. Thus, it was determined that this gentleman was already weary of life and committed suicide by jumping into the sea. Shao Weizu is likely his surname. In addition to reporting the incident to the local maritime public security bureau and notifying the Fujian branch of the shipping company and the Shanghai headquarters upon the ship's arrival in the Min River, we have also kept the recovered belongings in anticipation of family members claiming them. We respectfully submit this report, requesting your kind review and filing for record, and requesting your instructions to comply. Respectfully submitted, Yang Baokang, Captain of the Wanxiang Ship, Sanbei Shipping Company. It is reported that the Shipping Administration Bureau, after receiving the report, has been trying to locate the family members in order to notify them and enable them to claim the belongings.

Ping Pong Championship Dispute; Mediation Failed Yesterday; Court Orders Formal Lawsuit

The Xiangbin Cup Ping Pong Tournament, organized by the Racecourse Club, attracted many participants. After the battles, the Jiande Ping Pong Team and the Guangdong Ping Pong Team were tied for first place with 17 points each. Subsequently, the organizing committee of the cup competition scheduled the final match to be held on the evening of the 26th of last month at the Meifeng Branch Ping Pong Room. However, the members of the two final teams were participating in the China Ping Pong Association's pre-selection for the China-Japan Far East Ping Pong Tournament. Therefore, in accordance with Article 7, Section 5 of the Xiangbin Cup competition regulations, they sent a letter requesting a postponement. The committee replied one hour before the final match, denying the request. The Guangdong team arrived on time. The Jiande team, due to time constraints, was unable to gather its members and did not attend. The referee, Zhou Weixin, then ruled that Jiande had forfeited, placing them as runners-up. However, the organizing committee of the cup competition changed the referee's ruling and re-ruled that the Jiande team had withdrawn midway, and their scores would not be counted. The Jiande team argued that the withdrawal midway must be voluntary and cannot be forced. Moreover, as the regulations did not authorize the organizing committee to make any rulings, they believed that the ruling was not only illegal but also damaging to their reputation. Therefore, they engaged lawyers Yang Ruinian and Yin Jingyuan to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing the organizing committee members Li Hongde, Lu Xiwu, Shen Zhirui, Shen Ding, Lu Hanjun, Weng Shoufeng, etc., of abusing their authority and requested a preliminary mediation. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shi Meiyu of the First Special Court convened a mediation session in Civil Chamber Ten. The Jiande team was represented by Lu Xiu and their agents, lawyers Yin and Yang. Only Lu Xiwu appeared on behalf of the defendants. As the case concerned the future of the sports community, many people attended the court as observers. First, lawyer Yin stated the background, arguing that the withdrawal midway ruled by the defendants must be a voluntary application. The requester's request for postponement was fully compliant with the law and the notification was made, hence the other party had indeed abused their authority. Judge Shi then inquired of Lu Xiwu whether there was a basis for changing the referee's ruling of withdrawal midway. He replied that it was based on Article 7, Section 9 of the regulations. Judge Shi then declared that since the Jiande team and the Guangdong team had made a legitimate request for postponement, and the procedures and regulations had all been completed, it could not be considered non-compliant. As for the meaning of the term "withdrawal midway" in Article 7, Section 9, it applied only if the Jiande team had voluntarily requested to withdraw from the competition. How could that be used as a basis for the ruling? In the opinion of this judge, it would be better to resolve this game-related incident through reconciliation to avoid litigation. The best solution would be for the Jiande and Guangdong teams to compete again and achieve victory through strength, which would be the most appropriate. What do you think? However, Lu Xiwu insisted that this was unacceptable. Judge Shi repeatedly tried to persuade him, but to no avail. Judge Shi then declared that the mediation had failed and ordered the Jiande team to file a formal lawsuit.

Japanese Police Arrest Gold Smugglers; Customs Actually Assist Japanese Police in Escorting [Them] to Japan from Chinese Territory

On the 14th of last month, the Japanese ship Nagasaki Maru sailed from Japan to Shanghai. A Chinese passenger, Fu Zhilin, and a tea server, Qiu Zhihao, were carrying over 1,760 taels of gold bars, all hidden in two vests. As the passengers were disembarking, the police officer of the Japanese Consulate-General in Shanghai, upon receiving a telegram from Japanese authorities, stated that Fu and Qiu had violated Japan's gold export ban and should be immediately intercepted and sent to Japan for interrogation. The Japanese Consulate consulted with the Customs authorities and requested assistance in the search. As expected, Fu and Qiu were found among the passengers, and the gold-laden vests were discovered on their persons. Consequently, they were immediately taken to the Japanese Consulate for interrogation along with the witnesses. At that time, Fu and Qiu's families were not in Shanghai, so no one could rescue them, and they were allowed to be escorted back to Japan by the Japanese police. It is now reported that Fu and Qiu's families have heard the news and come to Shanghai, but their inquiries at various government offices have yielded no results. They know that they have been sent to Japan by the Japanese Consulate. However, it has been found that since the Nagasaki Maru has already arrived in Shanghai, it should not arrest people across borders and extradite them privately within Chinese territory. They are now engaging lawyers to petition the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urgently send a telegram to the Japanese Minister, requesting negotiations in accordance with the treaty.

Apricot Blossom House Bombing Case: Appeal by the Police Begins; Debate Concludes; Judgment to Be Announced Tomorrow

Zhang Guoxiang, a Sichuan native, is currently twenty-two years old. He used to serve as a volunteer soldier in Zheng Guilin's army. After retiring from the army, he came to Shanghai and joined the Red Blood Assassination Group, which aimed solely to warn treacherous merchants. On May 10th of this year, Zhang learned that the Apricot Blossom House Restaurant on Sima Road was selling Japanese goods such as shark fin, abalone, and dried shrimp. Therefore, at eight o'clock that evening, he threw a bomb as a warning. The bomb did not explode, and Zhang was immediately arrested and handed over to the First Special District Court. After the trial, it was considered that Zhang's actions stemmed from righteous indignation, and he was sentenced to three months of imprisonment. However, Mr. Boling, the Chief Attorney of the Legal Department of the Municipal Council, believed that Zhang Guoxiang had not thoroughly investigated whether Apricot Blossom House was selling Japanese goods. Even if Japanese goods were indeed used, he should not have dealt with it with drastic measures. His blind obedience was obvious. How could it be said to be motivated by righteous indignation? Therefore, he disagreed with the judgment and, together with the lead attorney, Li Zhishan, filed an appeal with the Second Branch of the High Court, requesting that the original judgment be overturned and a suitable judgment be made. Yesterday afternoon, Zhao Zheng, Jiang Shuzi, and Zhou Han, judges of the Second Branch of the High Court, held a hearing. Attorney Wang Yaotang appeared in court on behalf of the Municipal Council and stated the reasons. The court then interrogated Zhang Guoxiang and announced the conclusion of the debate, setting the judgment to be announced at 2:00 PM on the 15th.

Begging Unsuccessfully, Old Woman Injures People with Snake; Sentenced to Six Days of Detention

An old beggar woman, Pan Li, from Anhui Province, fifty years old, went to a certain butcher shop at No. 558 Minguo Road outside the Xiaobeimen of the French Concession at around 8 PM on the 5th of this month to beg unsuccessfully. She took out a poisonous snake she was raising to threaten people, causing the shop's local clerk, Zhu Jinbao, to be bitten on his right hand. The patrol arrested the old woman and brought her to the police station along with the poisonous snake. The snake was first killed, and then the old woman was sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday, Judge Qiu Huanying continued the trial in the Eighth Criminal Court. First, Gu Shouxi, the police attorney, presented the case and the investigation process. Then, the plaintiff, Zhu Jinbao, described how the defendant injured people with the snake. After the official questioned the defendant, he sentenced Pan Li to six days of detention. The number of days of pre-trial detention before the judgment is finalized shall be offset against one day of detention, as a warning.

Huang Jinrong: Establishes Caoxing Temporary Hospital

Mr. Huang Jinrong, a prominent figure in Shanghai, believes that Caohejing is located in the remote west of Shanghai and has never had a hospital, which is inconvenient for the local residents. The poor and sick, in particular, have no one to turn to. In view of this, Mr. Huang plans to build a Caoxing Hospital on the east side of his residence, the Huang Family Garden, with complete new equipment and employing senior doctors to provide some happiness for the local residents. The blueprints of the hospital have already been completed and construction will begin soon. However, with the hot summer approaching and the heat a concern, the spread of epidemics is a matter of urgency. As the area is far from the city center, there may be delays in seeking medical attention for emergencies. Therefore, a Caoxing Temporary Hospital will be temporarily established inside the Caohejing Theater in the east of the garden. Medicines will be given to the poor and sick free of charge, and a special Jinrong refreshing medicine water will be provided, which all residents of Caohejing can receive as a gift. The hospital affairs will be entrusted to the Shanghai Jishen Hospital, with Director Wang Zhenchuan in charge of everything. Well-known doctors will also be employed to be stationed in the hospital for regular consultations. The official opening will be on the 20th of this month.

The company ordered Jiang Amei (28 years old, from Pudong) and his assistant, Hu Shaoying (19 years old, from Suzhou), to drive car No. 12054 to Minhang for sightseeing. The four Westerners in the car were sent to Russian Hospital for treatment.

Carelessness at Cotton Shop in Dadongmen

It was founded in 1920 and has been in operation for fourteen years. The business has been able to maintain itself. His wife, Zhang, has a son and three daughters, and employs two partners. To their surprise, at around 5 AM yesterday morning, a loft downstairs in the shop suddenly caught fire. The police chief of the Third Precinct of the First District immediately informed the fire brigade to send vehicles to rescue. However, cotton is very flammable, so the fire was very fierce. Although the firefighters bravely rescued, the fire had already spread to the adjacent salted meat shop at No. 31, opened by Pan Caizhang from Ningbo, and the home of Liu Jingwan at No. 82, Alley 6, Mianjin Lane, causing heavy losses. The Third Collection of Biographies of Famous Chinese Historical Figures is Published; Edited by He Ziheng; Published by the Youth Association Press

The third collection of Biographies of Famous Chinese Historical Figures is published by the Youth Association Press at No. 131, Museum Road. It is edited by Mr. He Ziheng. Mr. He has been writing for the press for more than ten years and has a wide range of knowledge in philosophy, science, history, society, politics, economics, literature, and other fields, and has unique insights. Therefore, when editing this book, not only is the selection of characters not biased towards one side, but the recognition of the achievements and learning of famous people can also be maximized. According to Mr. He, the celebrities included are limited to those who meet the following six conditions: (1) those who are related to the rise and fall of an era and can influence history; (2) those who can expand territory and establish meritorious achievements; (3) those who have made great contributions to academic culture; (4) those who have extraordinary military genius; (5) great travelers who have traveled thousands of miles and endured hardships; (6) those whose morality and personality can be models for us. With these six conditions, the characters included will be comprehensive. This book starts from the Jin Dynasty and ends with the Sui Dynasty. The narrative is smooth, the writing is economical, and the annotations are detailed. Therefore, with this volume, readers can learn about the central figures in Chinese political and cultural history with minimal effort and time. At the same time, it can unintentionally improve the modern youth's Chinese language level. The price is one yuan. Those who want to buy it should hurry. The first and second collections were edited by Mr. Yu Muren and have already been published. The price of the first collection is 80 cents, and the second collection is one yuan.
