Letter

To the Editor:

Recently, I read the report on page 13 of the fourth page of your newspaper on the 10th of this month, in the local news column, with the headline "Local Tyrants Collude with Police Station Chief to Set Up Red Pill Organization," and the situation described in it is mostly inconsistent with the facts. The Chief of the Public Security Bureau, Mr. Wen, received two anonymous letters a few days ago, saying that there are many places in the area of the first station of the fifth district where red pills are sold and where people can smoke red pills. He immediately ordered the detective team to send detective leader Chen Fucai to investigate and arrest them strictly. At about 5:00 PM on the 7th of this month, detective leader Chen Fucai led many detectives to the station and asked to send police to cooperate in handling the matter. The chief of this station immediately sent police officer Tang Xixiang to go with them. They searched the addresses, but found nothing. Only in front of the building on Delin West Lane Road, Dongbaoxing Road, a smoking lamp, a pipe, and 25 red pills were seized on the spot, and Liu Ziye, Liu Linshi, Ni Bing, Shang Zhenjiang, and the police chief Yuan Fuchen and Wang Futian of this station were arrested. It was found that Shang Zhenjiang used to be a petitioning policeman at the Hong Kong Grand Theater. Later, the theater stopped performing and there was no need for a petitioning policeman, so he applied for cancellation in May, which was approved by this station.

The theater, and did not continue to ask for a petitioning policeman. According to police chiefs Yuan Fuchen and Wang Futian, they went to the tailor shop to get clothes and did not know that there was a place for people to smoke red pills. They happened to be there and were mistakenly involved in the arrest. However, although the police chiefs were police officers, even if there was no act of shielding or smoking red pills, there was still suspicion. In addition to handing over the police chiefs and all the witnesses to detective leader Chen Fucai to be taken to the bureau for interrogation, the chief of this station has already requested punishment for failing to supervise and detect the matter. He is deeply afraid that the rumors are false and will damage his reputation. He should communicate with you to correct it. This is respectfully addressed to the chief writer of Shenbao, the first station of the fifth district of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, June 12.

Incoming Mail: The Pilot Association Strives for Sovereignty and Rebuts Fallacies Again - Contribution from the Preparatory Committee of the China Pilot Association

The issue of China's recovery of pilotage rights has recently been opposed by the Chief Secretary of the Customs, who requested the government to amend the Interim Regulations on Pilotage Administration promulgated in September last year. This matter is of great importance and has aroused the attention of people across the country. Foreign newspapers have even made unreasonable propaganda to help their arrogance. The Preparatory Committee of the China Pilot Association in this city has translated an article from the China Review Weekly and announced it to the people of the country, refuting the arguments of foreign newspapers. The statement says: In the editorial of the April issue of the Oriental Affairs Monthly, there was a lengthy discussion on this issue. The paper cited many treaties signed between China and the powers as the basis for the debate, intending to confuse the readers who do not have accurate knowledge of the fact that foreign pilots at Chinese treaty ports, how and when they were formed, and how they were able to be compared with the hardworking and experienced Chinese pilots. It also criticized the newly promulgated pilotage management regulations of the Chinese government, nothing more than to echo the foreign pilots in Shanghai and increase their arrogance, and vaguely to speak for the consular corps. The monthly also indiscriminately attacked the declaration issued by the Preparatory Committee of the China Pilot Association with biased eyes and fabrication. The reporter distorted the treaties and added his own absurd personal views, intending to reap unilateral benefits.

Only facts can reveal the truth of a matter. Therefore, we must have a true understanding of China's situation a century ago in order to understand the treaties cited. For example, the treaty signed in Huangpu on October 14, 1884, is a document that, today, unless you refer to books of historical events, it can be said that no human can correctly interpret it. It must be known that China at that time had only five ports open to foreign trade, and foreign pilots had not yet reached these five ports. The entry and exit of all foreign ships at these ports depended entirely on Chinese pilots. However, for some reason, foreign ships often could not find Chinese pilots at will, and the pilotage fees were not determined. This is why the words "foreign ships have the right to hire pilots" and "the issue of pilotage fees should be regulated by Chinese officials in consultation with foreign consular corps" were inserted into the treaty. According to this, the so-called special regulations are only limited to the pilotage prices of Chinese people. Moreover, the pilot mentioned here clearly refers to Chinese people and foreigners, because China has no jurisdiction over foreigners. It would be ridiculous to say that the powers have therefore allowed China to exercise its jurisdiction over foreign pilots. Foreign pilots invaded Chinese ports far after China signed various treaties. Did not the late Sir Robert Hart report this fact to the Prime Minister's Office in 1867 (that is, the seventh year of Tongzhi)? From September 10 of the same year, including from May 30, 1866, to May 11 of the following year, there were a total of 203 pilots in all trading ports (including 103 Chinese, 40 British, 35 Americans, 10 Portuguese, 6 Danes, 6 Swiss, 2 Dutch, and 1 Austrian). The report also included a statement saying that although according to international law, the right to pilotage along the Chinese coast should be reserved for Chinese pilots only, according to the current situation, it is necessary to formulate temporary regulations to jointly manage Chinese and foreign pilots. Subsequently, Hart was ordered to draft these regulations, which were submitted to the Prime Minister's Office for approval and publication. Regarding this, there was no formal report on whether Hart had consulted with the ministers of the powers at that time. Even if there was, we cannot recognize it, because the regulations have become a form of agreement. The regulations clearly state that it is an order or regulation of the Prime Minister's Office, which is self-explanatory. We　know that only sacred laws have permanent properties, and these regulations of 1868 are already 66 years old, how can they be unchangeable? They should have been revised or re-ordered long ago. These regulations may have been reluctantly applied in the past, but in wartime, they endanger China's national defense. Moreover, since the implementation of the regulations, China has repeatedly signed conventions with the powers, the nature of which conflicts with the regulations. Therefore, they are no longer applicable today. Regarding the former item, an example is the Sino-French War of 1885. The following are excerpts from Mori's International Law and times,

In March 1885, the American Minister to Beijing, Yang, sent a telegram to the U.S. government regarding the Sino-French war at the time, saying, "The Chinese government opposes American pilots piloting French warships. Should it be stopped?" U.S. Secretary of State Bai Yade replied by telegram, "The intention is very good, but we cannot stop our citizens from privately taking risks to enter into private contracts, which are not prohibited by national law, nor can they be ordered to return to court by the consul." (To be continued)

Reading Q&A

How to Take Reading Notes 丨丨 Reply to Mr. Wang Shaohua

Previously, in the "Discussion on Reading Methodology," we briefly discussed the method of taking notes. Recently, Mr. Wang Shaohua has raised this question again in his letter, saying:

"......According to the elders, 'One must take notes when reading.' However, we know that taking notes is too uneconomical in terms of time. We must see a considerable extent before we become interested and start copying. How much time does this waste! We amateur self-learners value reading time as if it were gold. Moreover, as copying accumulates, the number of volumes will surely be considerable, and it will take a lot of time to look at them a second time. If we use this precious time to read other new books, we may gain more knowledge. Therefore, I feel that taking notes is a bit of a losing proposition, isn't it? But the elders say so, which makes me hesitate. Please, experienced gentlemen, give me some advice."

Indeed, many people feel that taking notes is too uneconomical in terms of time, and that reading other books with the time spent taking notes would be more beneficial. This kind of doubt is very common. However, the time spent taking notes is not wasted as you say, because while we should be aggressive in seeking knowledge, we must also take defense into account. Taking notes is a kind of rear-guard work, which systematizes and deepens the knowledge we have already acquired. Conversely, if a person cannot digest the knowledge he has obtained, extract the essence, eliminate the dross, and deepen it, then no matter how much he absorbs, it is like a marauding bandit trying to conquer the world, only attacking and not defending, which is useless. At most, we can only give him the label of "bookworm" that we discussed a few days ago. If we turn over the arranged type of a printing plate and mix them up, it will completely lose the function of the printing plate and become just a pile of type.

We now study and read books with much more convenience than the ancients. It is difficult to say that various sciences are still being created and continuously researched, but they have all established a system. Therefore, those who are new to a certain discipline should first read the introductory books of that discipline, and should thoroughly understand the general concepts of that discipline described in the introduction, and be able to remember the key points. Taking notes is to condense the vast aspects into a few short sentences, making it easier for you to remember and more economical for you.

Usually, most notes are taken using the summary method, extracting the important points of a book according to chapters, as if making a condensed version. Although this is the most clumsy method, it is very useful for beginners because it can train readers to grasp the core of each problem and concentrate the reader's memory, preventing waste.

A further method of taking notes is to avoid copying directly from the book as much as possible, which is to say that one can add one's own reflections. After we have finished reading a book, we should first clarify the content or object of study in that discipline, then carefully recall this content, and then start taking notes. Therefore, the effort spent on taking notes is 70% "thinking" and only 30% "writing." This is the principle of making summaries.

Next, we will discuss the specific methods of taking this type of notes. First, we can briefly describe the name, catalog, introduction, conclusion, page number, publication date, author's position, and time spent reading the book. Then, we can write down the content of the book, according to what we remember, in our own sentences. We do not have to adhere to the format of the original book; we should write according to our own convenience and opinions. The original book may divide a matter into several chapters due to length or separate the descriptions of one part from another for the sake of narrative convenience, but what we want to obtain is systematic knowledge and an overview. Therefore, we can abandon cumbersome and fragmented narratives and connect things that are discussed separately. As for the method of narration, the more concise the better, but important content cannot be omitted. If you are very interested, writing a little more is fine.

No matter what book it is, we cannot say that it is completely flawless. No matter how serious, it is common to not understand certain points when reading a book on a certain subject for the first time. In fact, readers' disagreements and doubts about the author's views, and the inability to thoroughly understand certain parts, are inevitable. If you encounter this kind of problem and cannot solve it, then don't over-repress your own views and blindly follow the book. After you have described the content, you can record these questions one by one. This can serve as the focus of your further research in the future. The reason why our interest in studying gradually increases is that the deeper the research, the more questions there are. To solve these problems, you must do further research, and therefore, your academic achievements will naturally become more in-depth. Therefore, this part is also very necessary in notes.

In short, taking notes helps you systematize and deepen the knowledge you have gained and keep it for future reference. Its main purpose is to focus on defense. The ancients said that doing scholarship is like "fighting a hard battle to the death," which is very reasonable. It would be a big mistake if we thought that the time spent on the defensive fortifications of the rear guard was not worth it compared to the offensive.

Record of the Opening of the Chinese Painting Exhibition in the Netherlands

Wang Chonghui, Liu Haisu, and others Participate in the Grand Ceremony

(Amsterdan dispatch) The Berlin Chinese Painting Exhibition was able to cause a sensation throughout Europe. It was not only praised by the German government and the public, but also attracted the attention of Britain, the Netherlands, Italy, Switzerland, France, and the Czech Republic. Various countries have requested to move the exhibition. The Netherlands was close to Berlin and was able to take the lead. The Dutch side was proposed by the Ministry of Education and led by Van Stoddard Bro, the director of the National Art Museum, and negotiated with Liu Haisu, the representative of our country, to make a decision. The Dutch committee members were Fan Aipi, Fan Lifer, Tuilai Shi, Fei Shire, Balenhai, Galoyis, Monteli, Bick, etc., a total of 20 people, with Van as the chairman and Ruiliduo, the president of the Sino-Dutch Association, as the vice chairman, responsible for handling everything. The opening date and exhibition location were originally coordinated to be held on April 22 at the Amsterdam Art Museum and on June 2 at the Hague Art Museum. However, due to the preparation time being too hasty, the opening ceremony was postponed to 3 pm on May 5 at the Amsterdam Art Museum. On May 3, our country's painter Liu Haisu arrived in the Netherlands from Hamburg with his works. Those who welcomed him at the station at that time included Van Stoddard Bro, the director of the Art Museum, Fei Shire, the secretary of the Art Association, Ruiliduo, the president of the Sino-Dutch Association, Ge Labo, the secretary, and dozens of overseas Chinese students in the Netherlands. Mr. and Mrs. Liu stayed at the America Hotel, and reporters and painters visited endlessly.

Venue Layout

The venue is on the first floor of the Amsterdam Art Museum. The museum's architecture is magnificent and grand, and it is extremely famous in Europe. The exhibits include many rare art history treasures. For example, more than 300 fine works of the modern Dutch master Van Gogh Ko's life are collected there. Other things can be imagined. Modern Chinese paintings are displayed on the lower level, divided into six major rooms. The first room also includes Chinese painting tools. All kinds of colors, inks, and paper from the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty to the present are complete. There are no fewer than 80 kinds of different brushes, which are extremely beautiful. The Dutch are all studying carefully. Another part displays finely printed picture albums, which print each of the fine works exhibited this time, a total of more than 60 pictures. The first book contains an article "Modern Chinese Painting" by Liu Haisu, which elaborates on the spirit and schools of Chinese painting. The Dutch people respect it very much. The first room contains more than ten works by Zhang Hongwei, Zhang Kunyi, Zhang Daqian, Zhang Ze, Zhang Shuqi, Zhao Ziyun, Chen Shaolu, Chen Shizeng, Chen Shuren, Chen Ziqing, and Mrs. Liu Cheng. The second room contains works by Qi Baishi, Jin Cheng, Qin Qingxue, Jing Hengyi, Qing Daoren, Zhou Yifeng, Zhu Jinjiang, Zhu Nanyun, Fang Rending, Wu Meihe, Du Qizhang, and Shi Zejing. The third room contains 15 large works by Liu Haisu, the Chinese representative, which are extremely magnificent and unrestrained. At the same time, masterpieces by Feng Chao Fu Tieniu, He Qiyuan, He Tianjian, Xia Jingguan, Xiang Zhu, Xie Gongzhan, Ren Bonian, Ren Weichang, Gao Qifeng, Gao Jianfu, and Xu Shichang are also listed. The fourth room contains works by Xiao Qianzhong, Hu Peheng, Hu Tinglu, Hu Youge, Huang Xiaoshu, Huang Banruo, Huang Binhong, Huang Shu'an, Rong Dakua, Gu Shusen, Li Qingsong, Li Qiujun, Li Fengting, Li Xiongcai, Li Gongci, and Li Zuhan. The fifth room contains works by Ling Wenyuan, Li Mianlin, Li Zuhan, Liang Kaishi, Liang Gongyue, Lin Qinnan, Lu Yifei, Lu Lianfu, Pan Tianshou, Bao Shaoyou, Pu Ru, Shang Shengbai, Shen Ziji, Su Wolong, Sun Luqing, Sun Menglu, Tang Jianyou, and Tang Guanyu. The sixth room contains works by Tang Dingzhi, Deng Chunshu, Di Pingzi, Ding Yunxuan, Bao Shaoyou, Wang Xianshao, Wang Yiting, Wang Shensheng, Wu Changshuo, Weng Yinruo, Wu Qinmu, Wu Qiunong, Wu Xingfen, Wu Hufan, and Yu Shaosong. The venue is lofty, the lighting is suitable, and the paintings are displayed in it, shining brightly.

Many People Attended

At 3 pm on May 5, the opening ceremony was officially held at the venue. On that day, the flag of the blue sky and white sun was raised above the soaring dome of the museum's main entrance, fluttering in the wind. At the entrance, the national flags of China and the Netherlands were hung alternately, which was extremely solemn. At that time, the Chinese representatives who attended the meeting included Liu Haisu and his wife, Dr. Wang Chonghui, Minister Jin Wensi and his wife, Consul General Feng Zhizheng and his wife, Mr. Ding Yuebo, Xu Jiaji, the party affairs instructor stationed in the Netherlands, and many overseas Chinese and students. The Dutch attendees included Amsterdam Mayor Fuli Tun and his wife, Mr. and Mrs. Le Bolun, representatives of the Ministry of Education, Mr. and Mrs. Wang Senke, representatives of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ruiliduo, President of the Sino-Dutch Association, Mr. and Mrs. Van Stoddard Bro, Director of the Art Museum, Mr. and Mrs. Fei Shire, Secretary of the Art Association, Nai Ci, Haitelin, Huakai Namen, Ci Huang, Luoteng, Ma Ai, Menton, Mattelmen, etc., directors of various museums, consuls of various countries, and reporters from various newspapers, totaling no fewer than 500 people, gathering celebrities from Europe and Asia, which was quite a grand occasion at the time.

Opening Ceremony

Visitors browsed through the rooms, and Wang, Liu, Jin, Feng, and others explained them one by one, all marveling at the wonder and beauty of Chinese painting. A lotus painting in ink by Mrs. Liu Cheng was purchased and collected by Van, the director of the Art Museum. At exactly 3 o'clock, Van Stoddard Bro led the crowd to the auditorium, stood up, and delivered the opening speech, saying that China can express extremely profound meanings with extremely simple brush and ink, full of charm and demeanor. It is truly what is called shaping in a moment and waiting to be interpreted for thousands of years. Then Le Bolun, the representative of the Ministry of Education, and Mayor Fuli Tun spoke, all praising the splendor of the Chinese painting exhibition this time, saying that the cultural communication will make the friendly relations between China and the Netherlands even more harmonious. Later, Liu Haisu, Minister Jin Wensi, and Dr. Wang Chonghui delivered speeches as representatives. Reporters from various newspapers took photos of Liu and others. The next day, each newspaper had a large article and criticism with great public opinion. The light was brilliant, shining all over Europe, and the national reputation was indeed not superficial. That evening, at 7 pm, the Amsterdam Art Museum Art Room hosted a banquet for Mr. Liu Haisu, and invited Minister Jin Wensi, Dr. Wang Chonghui, and Consul Feng Zhizheng to accompany him. More than 70 Dutch celebrities attended, and the etiquette was very grand.

Jiangsu Secondary School Graduation Joint Examination Committee Resolves Examination Methods in Detail The Committee Members are Isolated from the Outside World During the Examination Period Test Questions for Each Subject will be Determined by the 14th

Examination Committee Members have been Appointed, Including Cao Can, etc.

Zhenjiang dispatch: The Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Graduate Joint Examination Committee for the 22nd year held its second meeting in the conference room of the Department of Education. The attendees were Pan Zushu, Sun Buyuan, Cao Yin Can, Hu Huanyong, Zhang Jingfeng, Hong Beiping, Zhang Shunyu (Jing Dai), Zhang Qinliang, Ren Yitong, Xiang Shaoxuan, Chen Tianou, and Zhou Fohai. The Chairman of the Committee presided over the meeting. The meeting discussed the issue of confidentiality during the joint examination period and the issue of drafting and proofreading the test questions. It was decided to follow the previous session's method for the examination questions.

Confidentiality measures: (1) Each member should not go outside after entering the hall. (2) Visitors will not be received. (3) If there is an important matter that requires sending a letter, the letter should be unsealed and handed over to the first section for sealing and dispatch. (4) Incoming letters will be collected and forwarded by the first section. (5) Telephone calls will be made and received on behalf.

Drafting and proofreading of test questions: The drafting will be done by personnel hired by the department, except for the drafting of English. Proofreading will be done by each subject committee together with the secretary, paying attention to the following points: (1) Correct errors in handwriting. (2) Destroy blurry handwriting.

Test question style: Party Principles, Chinese, History and Geography will be written vertically. Mathematics, Physics and Chemistry, and Biology will be written horizontally. The following words should be marked in large letters on the test paper to remind the students: (1) Choose four questions to answer, except for Chinese. Do not answer more than four questions. (2) Copy the question first, then copy the answer. Copy the entire question. It was decided that the test questions for each subject should be submitted for review by the committee chairman by 5 pm on the 14th and then sent for drafting.

The committee members who will draft the test questions have been appointed: Cao Yin Can for Party Principles, Hong Beiping for Chinese, Zhang Jingfeng for Mathematics, Zhang Qinliang for History, Hu Huanyong for Geography, Pan Zushu for Physics, Sun Buyuan for Chemistry, Zhang Shunyu for Biology, and Ren Yitong for Foreign Languages. Examination Dates and Locations: This year's joint examination will be held in nine districts: Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, Shanghai, Nantong, Yangzhou, Xuzhou, and Nanjing. Each district will send a chief examiner to preside over the joint examination. It was also decided that the examination will be held simultaneously in all districts on June 20.

Shanghai Summer Children's Health Camp Enrollment

Registration begins today, school starts on July 6th

Camp location: Wusong Tongji University Middle School

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, Education Bureau, Children's Morning News, China Anti-Tuberculosis Association, and Children's Welfare Association, in view of the fact that Chinese children are physically weak, which greatly affects the nation and the people, are using the summer vacation to hold the "Shanghai Summer Children's Health Camp." Li Ting'an and Hu Shuyi from the Welfare Association, Zhang Junjun and Zhang Wei from the Anti-Tuberculosis Association, Wu Liguo and Sun Jiaqi from the Health Bureau, and Pan Gongzhan and Zhou Shang from the Education Bureau were appointed to organize a committee to carry out the project. It was decided that the Health Bureau would be responsible for medical affairs, the Welfare Association for administrative affairs, the Education Bureau for education, and the Anti-Tuberculosis Association for nursing. In addition to Dr. Sun Jiaqi, the school health director, two general practitioners, two nurses, two teachers, and six teaching assistants stationed at the camp day and night, nutritionists and other specialists such as Gao Jinglang, Zhu Shenzhi, and Jiang Zhaoju have been invited as consultants. Chen Heqin and others have been invited to provide guidance in education to facilitate progress. All children of citizens can enter the camp. The abridged rules are listed below:

Abridged Rules of the Camp

Name: Shanghai Summer Children's Health Camp. Purpose: This camp aims to use the summer vacation to improve children's physical and mental health and cultivate good hygiene habits. Organizers: This camp is co-organized by the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association, Children's Welfare Association, Education Bureau, Health Bureau, and Children's Morning News. Duration: This camp will run for six weeks from July 6th to August 16th. Location: Middle School Department of Wusong National Tongji University. Capacity: This camp is temporarily limited to 100 children. Age: Limited to children aged seven to twelve. Fees: This camp focuses on nutrition, so a food fee of twelve yuan and a tonic fee of three yuan will be charged, payable in full upon entering the camp. Those who leave or withdraw midway will not be refunded. All other fees are waived. Entry Procedures: (1) Healthy children may apply to join to improve their health. (2) Weak children should join to restore their health. (3) Children who wish to join must be examined by the camp's doctor and deemed qualified before they can be accepted. (Those with infectious diseases will not be admitted.) Instructors: The camp invites several experts in education, medicine, and other fields as consultants, and also employs resident doctors, nurses, teachers, teaching assistants, and administrative staff to be responsible for guidance and management.

Registration Begins

Time: June 1st to June 30th. Locations: (1) Anti-Tuberculosis Association, (2) Morning News Office, (3) Health Bureau South City Clinic. Parents must fill out an application form on behalf of their children when registering and pay a registration fee of three yuan, which will be deducted from the food fee upon entering the camp. Those who do not attend will not be refunded, and substitutions are not allowed. Items to Bring: Each student must bring the following items when entering the camp: two bed sheets, one comforter, one blanket, one pillow, one bath towel, one face towel, one mouthwash cup, two toothbrushes, one box of soap, one mosquito net, one summer hat, several sets of spare clothing, and other daily necessities. Physical Examination: A physical examination will be held from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM on July 1st. The camp reserves the right to refuse admission to anyone with a disease that could endanger the health of others. The registration fee will be refunded. Those who pass the examination will pay the remaining twelve yuan for food and receive an admission permit. On the morning of July 6th at 9:00 AM, take the camp's special vehicle to the camp to check the body and gather at the ping-pong room of the public sports field on Daji Road, West Gate.

Daily Routine

The daily routine is as follows: 6:00 AM wake up and wash, 7:00 AM outdoor exercise (approximately 25 minutes), 7:30 AM breakfast (followed by a walk), 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM outdoor games, 10:00 AM tonic, 10:30 AM to 11:30 AM art and natural science, 11:30 AM meditation or nap, 12:00 PM lunch (followed by a walk), 1:00 PM to 3:00 PM afternoon nap (outdoors or indoors), 3:00 PM to 4:00 PM review or calligraphy, 4:00 PM tonic, 4:30 PM to 5:00 PM free games, 5:00 PM to 6:00 PM bath, 7:00 PM dinner (followed by a walk), 8:00 PM lights out and sleep. Weekly Life: Various activities will be held once a week: (1) Group trips (time to be determined separately), (2) Parents' meeting (twice a month), (3) Weighing (twice a month), (4) Various competitions (kicking shuttlecock, patting ball, skipping rope, speech).

Japanese Observation Notes of the Chinese Children's Education Society (8)

— Zhou Shang

Colonization Education at the Immigration Training Center

Japan is a small island in the sea, with a territory less than one-seventh of that of our country, and the proportion of the population is difficult to compare. The population of Japan proper is about 60 million, with an average annual increase of about 750,000, and a military increase of 14 per 1,000. The population density per square mile is 260, excluding the major cities. Although there are many mountains, there is no mountain that is not green and no land that is not cultivated (when we passed through the villages of Beppu, every inch of land along the road was used for production), the cultivable land accounts for only one-seventh of the total area of the country, and the supply is still insufficient. Moreover, women are also working in society. Waiters in restaurants and hostels, ticket sellers in cars and trams, shop assistants in various shops, and even men's bathrooms all rely on women's services, which leaves some men unemployed. Last year, there were 45 million unemployed workers worldwide. The United States has a large population, and there are 14,000,000 unemployed. The next is Britain and Japan. Japan has 530,000 unemployed. If the proportion of the population is considered, the number should be astonishing. Although it is warm, they cry cold, and although the year is prosperous, they cry hungry. The whole country is in an uproar. No wonder its colonial policy has become more and more urgent. Therefore, the Ministry of Colonial Affairs was established, and the Colonial School was upgraded from the Taiwan Association School to the Colonial University. Its main target is none other than us. We should resist the aggression of airships and cannons, and we should also be careful to guard against the violence of colonial education.

The purpose of the Immigration Training Center is to train ordinary people to prepare for the necessary skills and knowledge to cultivate in South America, and to enable them to live and work in Brazil. The school was founded by the Ministry of Colonial Affairs and is directly managed by the Minister of Colonial Affairs, Ryuichiro Nagai. The training courses are nothing more than alphabets, simple language, etiquette, travel common sense, and medical common sense. The training period is extremely short, reportedly only eight days. Two trainings are scheduled each month, with 700 people each time, and more than 10,000 people each year. The most difficult thing during training is children who go with their parents. In this short period of time, it is very difficult to obtain good results.

To enter the Immigration Training Center, ordinary people must first see the government post advertisements everywhere to recruit immigrants to Brazil. The advertisements are large and numerous. We often see them when we travel in the interior. The advertisements also contain encouragement and explanations. Each person can get a subsidy of 50 yuan, and families are especially welcome to go, so that these people can become permanent colonists, open up a fixed paradise for the motherland, and provide a decent way out for the unemployed. When these people have a firm heart to go abroad, there will be so-called overseas lectures to engage in preliminary education. Then, the Overseas Immigration Association will handle the procedures and send them to the school. The most important condition for entering the school is a physical examination. If trachoma is found in a physical defect, they will definitely not be qualified to enter the school, because the United States refuses to allow trachoma patients to land. Trachoma is rarely seen in Europe and the United States, but it is especially common in Japan and also in our country. The world calls it "Eastern disease." They are all caused by infection. In addition to the physical examination, preventive injections are also given, fearing that they will get sick during the tropical journey. Preventive work can be said to be thorough.

The school has two four-story buildings with 860 beds. Each family can live in one room. There is one treatment room and one clinic. Medical treatment is completely free. There is one examination room for examining feces, etc. There is one supply yard for immigrants' supplies, and one men's and women's bathroom each. (According to Japan's influence from China and European and American customs in recent years, men's and women's bathing is completely separated. Even in inland hotels and public bathhouses, except for the beach sand baths in Beppu and the hot spring baths in Atami, men and women do not bathe together. Is this kind of reform evolution or degeneration? It all depends on the wise seeing wisdom and the benevolent seeing benevolence.) There are several bedrooms, and each bedroom has 12 beds. There are many unsanitary aspects. When we went to the top floor, we saw a large photograph of a ship, with the words "Pioneer of South American Immigration." This ship is the Kanagawa Maru. On March 10, Meiji 45, it carried 1,500 people and sailed from Kobe. The well-wishers were endless on the road. From this, we can see the general history of immigration to South America.

Vocational Education in Hyogo Elementary School

After visiting Kitano Elementary School and Kobe Immigration Training Center on the morning of April 4, the local municipal government hosted a lunch at the Central Pavilion. It is said that it is very rare for the government to host foreign guests. This time, we were very grateful for being treated so well. When we went to the banquet, we were afraid that they would ask unavoidable questions, so we were all on our guard. When we first arrived at the port, one or two newspapers had published reports on Sino-Japanese friendship, the Chinese government sending a large number of investigators to Japan, and saying that we were very surprised by the greatness of Nagasaki's construction. In fact, the China Children's Education Society is entirely a private legal group. The desolation and coldness of Nagasaki are no more than our Wusong. What is friendship? What is surprise? This kind of trick is nothing more than to cover the eyes and ears of the world and use it for external propaganda. Fortunately, the representative sent by the Kobe Municipal Government that day was still witty, starting with perfunctoriness and ending with perfunctoriness.

Jinan University held two demonstration matches in soccer and basketball yesterday afternoon to celebrate its eighth anniversary. The soccer game started at 4:00 PM. The players on both sides had not played for a long time, and their skills were rusty. Lawn Tennis League: China Club Beat French Business Club Yesterday | Result: 9 to 6, Prospects Quite Optimistic | Defu and Pan Lifeifei Beat Qiu Feihai and Wang Wenzheng

In yesterday's lawn tennis league match between China Club and French Business Club, it was expected beforehand that China was extremely dangerous. Shen Bao National Products Weekly

Words of Contribution

National Product Industry Should Pay Attention to Foreign Trade

— Yang Yan

The outlet for national products is not only in various parts of the country, but should also be promoted in foreign markets. In this era of economic panic spreading across the world, every country is desperately promoting the sales of its products, using all kinds of methods and thinking of all kinds of plans, both seeking to boost the sales of its own products and restricting the import of foreign goods. Therefore, even Japanese goods, which are best at exploiting every opportunity, are now encountering obstacles everywhere, facing difficulties in finding outlets. In this situation, the only way for our national product manufacturers to save themselves is to first avoid domestic competition and focus on foreign trade. It must be understood that infighting and jealousy among peers are past bad habits that should absolutely not exist today. Everyone in the national product industry should stand together, taking the same steps to respond to the current crisis. Through cooperation among the same industry, and even cooperation among different industries, striving for lower costs and exquisite products, China's national products will not find it difficult to compete in foreign markets in a few years, perhaps three to five. Recently, Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo went to Nanyang to investigate industries. His task was not only to connect the country's production sector with foreign consumers, so that our national products can expand their market, but also to enable overseas Chinese in Nanyang and the local government to have a kind of appropriate exchange. After returning to China, Chen strongly stated that Nanyang's commerce has considerable development prospects, and that most of the local overseas Chinese lean towards the motherland, especially being very enthusiastic about national products, unanimously happy to use them; unfortunately, national product manufacturers still do not have strong organizations, so that they cannot fully expand the foreign market. Overseas Chinese in Nanyang all say that they are very eager to consume more national products, but the goods often do not suit the needs of the local area, such as the size of fabrics, the decoration of goods, and the psychology of users. This is the reason why national products cannot sell well in Nanyang. After hearing Chen's report, our manufacturers should uniformly pay attention to the selection of products, catering to the preferences of various places in Nanyang, in order to expand outlets, especially hoping that many manufacturers will jointly go to various places in Nanyang to conduct practical investigations, to establish friendly contacts, and bring various products to hold exhibitions, study their preferences, meet their needs, improve manufacturing, and facilitate transportation. Manufacturers can imitate the Japanese approach, specializing in the production of goods that sell well in Nanyang. If this can be done, then how difficult is it for our national products to compete with Japan and other countries in foreign countries? It depends on the vision and courage of the manufacturers.

Qingdao Industrialists Join Hands to Promote National Products

— Sun Choucheng

The Qingdao Industrial Inspection Group came to Shanghai on May 16th, and arranged a daily schedule to visit various factories, lasting for over ten days. Choucheng and Mr. Wu Shuchen, an executive of the Chinese Industrial Federation, accompanied them. Therefore, all the banquets in various places were also on the list of invitees. However, the talks at the banquet in Jue Lin Vegetarian Restaurant on the 24th were the most valuable.

On that day, the Chinese Vocational Education Society, the Chinese Vocational School, the Chinese Chemical Industry Society, the Chinese Iron Factory, the Chinese Enamel Factory, the American-Asian Silk Weaving Factory, and the Wuhe Weaving Factory jointly hosted a public banquet. Mr. Huang Renzhi was recommended to deliver a welcome speech. In addition to praising the members of the inspection group for their enthusiasm in promoting national products, Mr. Huang also said that during this period of severe national crisis, the four words "Industrial Development to Save the Nation" should be firmly adhered to and not forgotten by the industrial sector. The connection between the industrial sectors of Qingdao and Shanghai has been more than a day. Both sides have formed inspection groups to visit factories, and Shanghai has even gathered products from various factories to open an exhibition in Qingdao last year. All achievements were the best compared to other places. From this point alone, it can be seen that the Qingdao compatriots' enthusiasm for using national products is better than other ports. The so-called connection is not the connection between the Zhang and Li families, nor the connection between the A and B matters, but should have a concrete organization, roughly divided into two types: (1) the connection between the same industry and the same industry, regardless of region, and (2) the connection regardless of whether it is the same industry or not, limited by region. I hope that the gentlemen of the inspection group will not just come to Shanghai to visit factories this time, and then return to Qingdao to make a report and be done with it. They should take this opportunity to think of a concrete organization. This matter is not only related to industry, but also to international politics. Starting from today, industrial leaders from Qingdao and Shanghai should start joining hands to work hard for the development of industry and the promotion of national products, in order to plug the loopholes and save the country's fate. The head of the War Police Corps said in his reply: "Universal Education and Industrial Development" are the key to saving the country today. The other day, I visited the Chinese Vocational School and saw that the students used both their hands and brains, were strong and hardworking, which was different from ordinary schools. It can be seen that the seniors present have a thorough understanding of industrial research, which is admirable. The twentieth century is an era of commercial warfare. Qingdao was previously in the hands of Germany and Japan, and there was no way to talk about industry. After the recovery, it was gradually reorganized, and there were still many foreign factories. Taking the yarn factory as an example, Mr. Wu Bosheng, the deputy head of our group, has a Huaxin Yarn Factory in Qingdao, while the Japanese have six yarn factories, engaging in dumping. It goes without saying that the situation is difficult with one against six. Fortunately, the workers in Qingdao all have patriotic hearts. In the previous year, foreign factories went on strike for several months, while Chinese factories worked as usual. Cooperation between labor and management can resist foreign aggression. I hope that Shanghai entrepreneurs will go to Qingdao to open factories, to be a new force, and fight with foreign merchants. Qingdao is not only beautiful and convenient for transportation, but also all workers have simple lives and can endure hardships. In the past, they went to the three northeastern provinces to make a living, but since the September 18th Incident, they have all returned to Shandong. There are more people than jobs, and they only seek to be warm and full. The wages are much lower than in Shanghai. Mr. Huang's proposal is very insightful. I would like to use the host's wine to thank you all. Then, Mr. Ren Shigang proposed that both the guests and the hosts should introduce their history, as a preliminary hand-in-hand. On the guest side, Mr. Jingtang was asked to tell each member's personal business one by one, and the introduced person stood up so that everyone at the table could recognize them. On the host side, Mr. Pan Yangyao was asked to introduce them in order, and he also explained everyone's past history in detail. This method is more effective and interesting than exchanging business cards and exchanging pleasantries. Afterwards, Mr. Wu Bosheng said that running a factory should not only think about making profits, but should also have a compassionate heart, so that fellow compatriots can all have food to eat. Everyone said that this is what the Buddhists call having no ego. If we can be like this, we can all reach the other shore. Speaking Buddhist language in a Buddhist place, the scenery and emotions are intertwined, and everyone is happy.

Dragon Boat Festival and National Products

— Zhang Zhang

The Dragon Boat Festival is here, really, the Dragon Boat Festival every year, in one more day, it is coming again! In the few days before and after the Dragon Boat Festival, our Chinese custom is to give gifts to each other. Originally, this kind of custom, from the perspective of enlightened people, should of course be eliminated and abolished. However, in the minds of ordinary people, it seems that they still firmly refuse to break it, especially the housewives who are in charge of household affairs. It is even more difficult to eliminate and abolish. This is really a wasteful thing! From the perspective of reducing the national economy, of course, we think it is unreasonable. However, if we stand from the perspective of promoting national products, it is an excellent opportunity and time to promote national products. As long as housewives can understand the importance of promoting national products and purchasing national products, and understand that promoting national products and purchasing national products is the housewife's natural duty and work hard to implement it, then on this day of the Dragon Boat Festival, we can call it the National Products Festival. This is really an issue that housewives and the national product industry should jointly pay attention to.

How can housewives promote national products and purchase national products during the Dragon Boat Festival? My opinion is as follows:

(1) Gifts of national products: I think that giving gifts during the Dragon Boat Festival can be saved as much as possible. If it is unavoidable, then the goal of giving gifts to relatives and friends should be to purchase national products. At the same time, when purchasing, you must go to reliable national product factories and national product companies, so that you will not be wronged and deceived. Otherwise, the deceptive methods of unscrupulous merchants are endless. Maybe we will be deceived by the altered enemy goods!

(2) Receiving gifts of national products: The meaning of giving gifts is only to express the feelings between relatives and friends! However, there is also the meaning of promoting national products in it. Therefore, those who give gifts must purchase national products to give to relatives and friends. However, those who receive gifts should especially pay attention to whether the gifts sent are national products? If they are national products, then you can thank them a few times and accept them. If they are not national products, we can return a piece of paper to him, explaining the reason for not accepting. If everyone can do this, then those who send non-national product gifts will definitely not buy foreign goods to send people next time. This effect is really great. I hope that all Chinese intellectuals will implement this method and implement this proposition, which will be of great help to the future of the national product movement and the promotion of national products.

Alas! The Dragon Boat Festival is really a good opportunity to promote national products. I hope that everyone will pay attention to this issue together, to create one more outlet and one more opportunity for national product promotion.

Thoughts on "Japanese Goods Encountering Obstacles Everywhere"

— Xuan Wan

"Japanese goods," "Japanese goods," this painful and terrifying term, naturally all of us Chinese people with a little bit of blood, whether we see it in the newspaper or hear it from friends, will always stand up with an attitude of anger and a psychology of hatred. There is no other reason than that it has given us a very deep historical proof of its malice, and we can definitely recognize it as a kind of most poisonous snake. If its disturbance is truly rampant, it is all enough to endanger the collapse of our social economy and the stability of the national economy and people's livelihood. Regarding this monster's daily actions, it particularly arouses our attention and 120% attention.

Recently, we have seen in the newspaper a headline that "Japanese goods are encountering obstacles everywhere." It turns out that its content is this: "The Egyptian government, in view of the recent drastic dumping of Japanese goods, with the most resolute attitude, ordered its consul in Kobe, Mr. Houqi, to protest to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, intending to adjust Japan's one-sided trade. At the same time, the Consul of Haiti in Kobe, Mr. Gerj, also notified the Osaka Chamber of Commerce and Industry to urge Japanese merchants to purchase Haitian products in order to adjust the balance of trade between the two sides. Otherwise, Haiti will prohibit the import of Japanese goods, with an even tougher attitude. In addition, Jamaica and other British colonies have also increased tariffs one after another, banning the import of Japanese cotton fabrics, expressing unified action." From here, we can more deeply see the fierceness of Japanese goods dumping in the world market, but the news of the 27-nation boycott of Japanese goods movement heard a few months ago and the current "Japanese goods encountering obstacles everywhere" is really his most serious revenge.

However, here, we have three very deep thoughts. Originally, the countries of the world are not easy to invade. None of them are willing to be subjected to the blitzkrieg of dumping with a meaning of resistance, and they have already raised tariffs, foreign exchange management, import restrictions, and implemented anti-dumping duties to make the most powerful sanctions. But looking back at our country, the flooding of enemy goods is still the same. According to yesterday's newspaper, in the Sino-Japanese trade in April, the import of Japanese goods has an even more sharply increased trend compared to March. They have built high and hard barriers to make Japanese goods encounter obstacles everywhere, but we are just like mercury spilling on the ground. The enemy goods are rolling in and are ubiquitous, causing the national product industry to be even more threatened and unable to breathe forever. What is the reason? It is a "painful mystery"!
