Spring and Autumn

Imperial Fragrance Drifting Record

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

Before the collapse of the Manchu Qing Empire, there were certain laws and regulations for clothing. All officials and their wives had to obey them. However, these laws and regulations were not inhumane, but simply prescribed different styles of clothing according to the seasons of spring, summer, autumn, and winter. And each season was represented by a flower. In winter, the yellow wintersweet flower was used; in spring, the peony flower; in summer, the lotus flower; and in autumn, the chrysanthemum flower. All the female officials in the palace and the wives of those courtiers outside the palace had to embroider the flower representing the season on the clothes they wore each season if they wanted to embroider flowers. For example, in spring, they had to embroider peonies, otherwise not only would it be out of fashion, but they would also be charged with disobeying the imperial decree!

In addition to the floral decorations on the clothes, the style of the clothes was also prescribed according to the different seasons. For example, in winter, although everyone had to wear fur clothes, sometimes they only had to wear fur clothes with exposed fur edges, while other times they had to wear fur clothes that were fully lined with fur. Even the types of fur were not all the same. There were four types prescribed, all of which were changed according to the warmth of the weather. These four types of fur were: silver fox, gray fox, fox, and sable.

At the beginning of winter, the Empress Dowager would issue an edict, which was usually issued overnight. This edict would say something like "From tomorrow onwards, everyone should wear fur." Of course, the content of this edict would not be so simple. According to the rules, there would be a long official article, but in summary, it would not go beyond the meaning of these two sentences. Therefore, every courtier probably had a lot of clothes hidden away, because when the Empress Dowager's edict was issued, they would have to put on their fur clothes when they went to court the next day, no matter what. If they were not prepared in peacetime, how could they have time to do so temporarily! (57)

The So-Called Scientific Spirit Medium

— Luo Er

Several male and female relatives and friends gathered together to discuss scientific spirit mediums.

Mrs. Yu wanted to summon the spirit of her deceased nephew to talk to her because she missed him. In particular, she wanted him to say what he wanted to talk to her about when he was dying.

Mr. Lu Er solemnly told a news story about the miracle of the spirit medium, which was miraculous!

"A colleague once asked the spirit medium for the winning number of the fifth phase of the aviation lottery. As a result, he got the answer of the number five at the end. After the lottery was drawn, this colleague did not win, but he also made a small profit, because he won a lot of same-number awards at the end one and end two. If you say it's not effective, then what is this all about!"

After hearing this, Mr. Fang Da shouted repeatedly, "There is also one of my classmates, which is even more strange. He asked the spirit medium to summon a living friend to talk. When the conversation was over, he announced that he had invited a living person, and everyone couldn't help but burst into laughter. At that moment, the spirit medium suddenly jumped ten feet high and heavily hit him on the head. What do you say!"

Mrs. Yu opened her eyes wide and kept shouting, "Tsk! Tsk! Tsk! Effective! What an effective spirit! It should be hit! Good hit!"

"It's better to believe it exists than not to believe it exists." Mr. Lu Er nodded repeatedly, saying in his native dialect.

Mr. Fang Da was the most curious. The next day, he bought a pair of spirit mediums, and in the living room, he begged the immortals, invited the gods, and summoned souls, so sincere that he could touch heaven and earth.

Three fingers of different shapes pressed tightly on the spirit medium. Wait five minutes, no movement, wait ten minutes, no movement, wait fifteen minutes, no movement. Six eyes gradually turned red, and three fingers seemed to be trembling, but the spirit medium's body was pressed stiff.

Bang! Nothing! Dangling! Dangling! The spirit medium was angry, and suddenly jumped more than ten feet high, threw itself into the spittoon and died.

Only then did Mr. Fang Da angrily scold, "Damn it, damn it, making fun of me!"

Unfilial Son Reads the Classic of Filial Piety

— Qing

Li Jinfang, the magistrate of Funing County, was the county magistrate who was admitted with the first place in Jiangsu Province. Since he became the magistrate of Funing, his political achievements have been quite good. Yesterday, a friend from Funing, Mr. Li, told me about Magistrate Li's punishment of the unfilial son, which was very interesting. I will record it as follows:

In the east city of Funing County, there is a Dong XX, who has served in the education sector and can be regarded as an intellectual. But he has a bad habit, which is that he is unfilial to his parents. He insults his father at will and scolds him arbitrarily. His father only has one son, so he doesn't care about him. Who knew that he would actually make progress and start asking his father for debt? Probably last year, he wrote a letter to his father, with the heading "XX sees the letter:" (his father's name) and the signature "written by the old master," with the content that he should quickly repay the money, otherwise he should write a note of debt. If he is unable to repay in the future, he must turn into a donkey to repay the debt of the old master in the next life. At that time, his father was very angry and immediately reported him to Magistrate Li for unfilial piety. Magistrate Li's purpose was to preserve the old morality, so after hearing about this, he grabbed him and put him in prison. He also bought a Classic of Filial Piety for Dong XX to read, and only released him after he repented. It is said that he is no longer like he used to be to his father!

There are many unfilial sons everywhere! If they can all be treated like this, it would be a very gratifying thing!

Northeast Four Company Commanders

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 30: Watching the Mourning Geese Bury Themselves to Guard the Territory; Bullets Pierce Strong Arms, Sprinkling Blood to Dye the Lonely City

At this time, he received the battalion commander's order to build up the village and the defensive works outside the south gate. Outside this south gate, there were already two temporary trenches. Fang was always afraid that the enemy's tanks would not be easy to resist, so he ordered Ziqiang to lead his own company of brothers to dig another dry trench outside the south gate, with branches and deer forks piled on the trench to block the enemy. Ziqiang stood on the earthen slope, looking down at his brothers digging the trench. Accidentally, he looked up and saw the old people and children of the village inside the stronghold walking towards the entrance. The old man he had entrusted was also walking slowly among them. He seemed to see Ziqiang standing on the slope paying attention to him, so he reached into his arms and took out a letter, waving it repeatedly in front of him. It seemed that he meant to indicate that he could take the letter to him. Ziqiang had nothing else to say, just watching him from afar. Because if he raised his hand to show anything, it would be seen by his brothers. He felt that he could not concentrate on military affairs, and still had to think about his family, which was a kind of laziness, so he did not move, but only watched with his eyes as if he did not know about this at all. The brothers who were working on the slope were all waiting quietly for the company commander to command. Now that they saw the company commander only staring at the road back to the south, maybe they were looking at the old people and children walking forward and thinking of home? Because of this, those who were carrying earth outwards, holding manure baskets, did not know where to pour it, and were also looking forward. Those who were digging earth with hoes on the slope, although they could not see the top, were also holding their hoes and raising their heads, looking up at the slope. One was like this, and everyone inevitably stopped working. Ziqiang accidentally turned his head and saw everyone in this situation, thinking to himself, this is terrible, a momentary negligence of five minutes almost caused a collective slack. So he did not question his brothers, but jumped down the slope, picked up a hoe, raised it high, and dug ten times. (408)

The Dumpling Seller's Child

— Liancheng

Still in the darkness of early morning, a sorrowful voice cries, "Dumplings! Dumplings! Dumplings!" from the mouth of a small child. This sound doesn't dissipate until the sun is high and the young masters and misses rise from their beds. It's been like this for almost a year, regardless of cold or heat, rain or shine.

Every time I hear this sound, I instinctively curse, "If you don't need sleep, why disturb others' sleep?"

Although I hate him intensely, I never have the courage to stop him when he cries out.

But for the past few days, I haven't heard this sound. I was glad, thinking I could finally sleep peacefully. It truly felt like regaining something precious. But things in this world rarely go as expected. Just as I was celebrating the end of the sleep disturbance, the "Dumplings! Dumplings!" sound disappeared, and another sound disrupting sleep appeared in its place. But compared to the previous one, this new sound is even more sorrowful and even more unbearable. The previous sound was a child's voice; now it's a woman's. Before, it was the selling cry of "Dumplings! Dumplings!"; now it's the weeping cry of "My child, my flesh!"

Ah! I've had enough! I've had enough! Bring back the original sound! But alas! The child no longer cries out.

Traces of the Art

Random Jottings from a Southern Tour: Street Scenes in Fuzhou

— Shazhou

Fuzhou is a famous city in South China. It has a long street that stretches for several miles, with modern buildings lining both sides. Radios in the shops play popular Min tunes all day long to attract customers. Cars used by provincial officials to save time and shorten distances speed along smooth cement roads, with horns blaring everywhere. Combined, the unique clamor of the city forms a modern symphony. Women, too, are unwilling to lag behind; their clothing styles keep up with advanced Shanghai, and their demeanor and physique carry a southern charm. But is Fuzhou really as prosperous as people imagine? No, no, this massive city hasn't escaped the pervasive economic panic. The shadow of recession and decline has already enveloped it, just like many other cities.

Those who have been to Fuzhou probably know that Fuzhou's prosperity is simply based on commercial economy. Citizens have more opportunities for consumption, and less opportunity for production. Although there are many barefoot working women on the streets, this is not enough to hide the hunger of many stomachs. Many social evils are caused by poverty. In the park at dusk, there is no shortage of virtuous women taking leisurely strolls. But at the same time, under the bright electric lights, powdered-faced women are searching for the fate of their families. The power of hunger has made them bow their heads in helplessness. When a wave of despair washes over them, how dare they wail? They can only cast their weary gaze at the cement heads, because only the cement heads understand them.

Foreign Languages

"Nü xi ben ma? Xi gui wan? A sai a sai, a lü a lü." It's really maddening, this Fuzhou language. Not only Fuzhou, but the languages of all of Fujian are like foreign tongues. Hearing them makes your brain ache.

Those who arrive in Fuzhou for the first time—even those who have lived there for quite some time—all experience the difficulty of not being able to communicate. For example, if you want to hire a rickshaw, you can shout "Rickshaw! Rickshaw!" until your voice shakes the heavens, but the rickshaw puller acts as if he hasn't heard anything. Some even stare at you blankly, thinking you're suffering from some kind of madness. Buying things, asking for directions… isn't it all just as difficult? But the effort is often in vain. The other person will never understand what you mean, just as you can't understand them. A friend said to me, "We can accept not understanding foreign languages, but for Chinese people to not understand other Chinese people is unreasonable and unacceptable." But unreasonable things abound, and there are many of them. Isn't this a great disgrace to our own country?

I used to hear people say that the Fujian language sounds like bird calls, and I didn't dare believe it. Because I imagined that the Fujian language was at most like the difference between Northern Mandarin and Shanghai dialect. Although the accent is different, the pronunciation of the words only differs by half, so there is some resemblance when spoken. But in retrospect, "eat" is called "xi ben," and "yes" is called "a sai a sai." How many thousands of miles is that from the common Mandarin used throughout the country? It would not be an exaggeration to call this a foreign language.

But should this Min language, which is like a foreign tongue, be allowed to exist forever?

The Dingguang Pagoda

From any open field in Fuzhou, looking towards the city, as long as there are no tall buildings or dense forests obstructing your view, you will surely see two straight columns of smoke protruding into the sky amidst the deep and vast patterns woven by the multi-colored rooftops. They stand out like cranes among chickens, one white and one black. Although the black one also stings the eyes of tourists, it is often overlooked in conversation and memory. The white one is proud, like the White-Robed Avalokiteśvara, and is often on people's lips. This is the Dingguang Pagoda that I'm going to talk about.

Like giant beetles, many ancient steles stand on the mountain, and poems commemorating Qi Jiguang are carved on the rocks. Looking down from the mountain, you can see the secluded Chan rooms of the White Pagoda Temple. But looking up again, you see the majestic appearance of the Dingguang Pagoda.

An old monk stands at the pagoda gate, asking tourists for a few copper coins to enter the pagoda. Entering the pagoda is extremely dark. Following the winding staircase upwards, from the first floor to the seventh, there are compassionate Buddhist images painted on the walls and inscriptions written by famous people. However, trivial words like "On X month X day, I came for a visit with my wife" are also mixed in. Even worse are twisted poems like "High mountains have good water, flatlands have good flowers." Such a beautiful scenic spot has been defiled by vulgar visitors. But the majestic appearance of the White Pagoda still stands proudly in the muddy waters of the city.

The outer edge of the pagoda has stone railings on each floor for people to lean on and enjoy the view. From there, you can overlook the scenery of the entire city. Nuns in the foreign church are walking with their heads bowed, and girls playing ball make light laughter.

The handrail of the White Pagoda spirals upwards from three sides, reaching the top, and can be said to be the epitome of science. But those who speak only mention the skyscrapers of Russia or the high-rise buildings of America. The greatness of our own country's architecture is always ignored. How much does this cause people to lament and complain?

Page 17

Free Talk

Toys

— Mizi Zhang

This year is Children's Year. Because I remember this, I often look at the toys made for children.

In the foreign goods stores next to the road, sporadic small items are hung up, with labels indicating that they are shipped from France, but I have seen the same goods in Japanese toy stores, only the price is cheaper. On shoulder poles and in small stalls, rubber bubbles that gradually inflate as you blow into them are sold, stamped with the words "Completely Domestically Made," indicating that they are manufactured in China. However, Japanese children also play with rubber bubbles with the same stamp, which should be made by them.

Large companies have weapon toys: command swords, machine guns, tanks... However, even children from wealthy families rarely play with them. In the park, foreign children gather sand into round piles, and insert two short tree trunks horizontally. This is clearly creating armored gun vehicles. Chinese children, on the other hand, have pale and thin faces, hiding behind adults, shyly and surprisedly watching, wearing extremely refined long gowns.

In China, there are many toys for adults: concubines, opium pipes, mahjong tiles, light rain, scientific spiritualism, Vajra Dharma assemblies, and more, keeping everyone busy. There is no time to think about children. Even though it is Children's Year, and even though we experienced the ravages of war the year before last, there hasn't been a memorial keepsake created for children. Everything is still copied as before. Then next year it won't be Children's Year, and the situation is easy to imagine.

However, people from Jiangbei are geniuses at making toys. They use two bamboo tubes of different lengths, dyed red and green, connected in a row. Inside the tube is a spring, and there is a handle on the side. When you shake it, it makes a rattling sound. This is a machine gun! It is also the only creation I have seen. I bought one on the edge of the concession, and walked down the road shaking it with my child. Civilized Westerners and victorious Japanese people mostly give us a contemptuous or pitying bitter smile.

However, we walk down the road shaking it without shame, because this is a creation. Since the year before last, many people have scolded the people of Jiangbei, as if this is not enough to show their nobility. Now they are silent, and that nobility is also vague and boundless. But the people of Jiangbei have created crude machine gun toys, using their strong confidence and simple talent to compete with civilized toys. I think they are more worthy of praise than those who buy the latest weapons from abroad, although perhaps some will give me a contemptuous or pitying sneer because of this.

Beishan and Temple Fair

— Xicun

丨Miscellaneous Writings from Jilin, Two丨

Speaking of Beishan, it can be said that it is the most beautiful place in Jilin. The mountain is not big, nor too high, lying on the northwest corner outside the city. The mountain has tall trees that shade the sun, scattered and mixed low forests, and green lawns like carpets, while also contrasting with red and yellow sandy roads and rows of rocks. There are also carved palaces and platforms by craftsmen, but there is no shortage of thatched huts and grass huts built at will by rural elders. Behind the mountain slope, there are several tilted pagoda tops, closely adjacent to the westernized water pool, as if deliberately declaring themselves as representatives of Eastern and Western cultures. The sandy road, winding and winding, disappears from the foot of the mountain into the mountain. Large and small tea sheds and book stalls are lined up along the road. There are also several sheep intestines trails. During the summer and autumn plum festivals, when the sun sets and dusk falls, people generally want to spit out the stuffiness in the city and cultivate their spirits, they always come to Beishan to play. On the mountain, listening to the bells of the temple, enjoying the cool breeze of the evening, and looking out over the Songhua River, gradually rising and thickening, and the red glow reflected in the western half of the sky, is a kind of lighthearted feeling.

At the foot of the mountain, a large open space is spread out, and next to the open space is a clear pool of water, dotted with clumps of green cattails and aquatic plants. A stone bridge climbs over the water, which is the main road between the city and the mountain. Willow trees are everywhere, always liking to wrinkle the water with the wind. The Ji-Hai Railway meanders from the northeast to the southwest along the water's edge, close to the mountain roots. Therefore, this beautiful landscape of mountains, rivers, and plains is often sprinkled with clusters of coal smoke from locomotives.

Every year, Beishan has a temple fair, and everyone in the province knows the grandness of the temple fair. The temple fair day is the twenty-eighth day of the fourth lunar month, which is the "main day", plus the twenty-seventh and twenty-ninth two "auxiliary days", there are three days in total.

A few days before each temple fair, the railway bureau has to add trains, and the ticket prices are discounted, what a rare opportunity! Farmers from outside the township, in order to bargain, in order to go to the provincial capital to visit the scenery, and some people in order to burn incense and fulfill their vows in the temple, at this time, would rather sacrifice a few days of work in the fields, and are willing to take this opportunity to play for a few days.

Speaking of the temple fair itself, it is actually a move that wastes money and time. In addition to some temporary markets being added at that time, and some large and small stores taking the opportunity to do business, the only other thing is burning incense. All the people who visit the mountain and attend the fair will spend some money.

Although the temple fair is once a year, in 1932, the provincial administrative authorities exceptionally ordered it to be stopped, because the area was not peaceful, and the volunteer army lurking around Jilin City could attack the provincial capital at any time, and the temple fair suffered an unfortunate fate as a result. To be honest, at that time, people really didn't have the mood to visit temples and attend fairs: those living in the city were panic-stricken, and the villagers were also living a life of "not knowing whether they would live or die tomorrow," which can be said to be a gift given by the great turmoil.

But the situation in 1933 was different. Because the Japanese troops had somewhat suppressed the volunteer army. So, this year's temple fair was specially promoted and held, becoming a tool for the "Cooperation Society" to promote "Royal Wayism". Using the temple fair to carry out political propaganda is probably the first time since there has been a temple fair in Beishan.

The so-called propaganda by the temple fair is so simple that it makes people laugh when they hear it. It only relies on Japanese planes to scatter some leaflets and slogans in the sky over the mountain and the ground below. Here is a leaflet with the fewest words:

"The Gift of the New Country"

"Golden spears are sure to bring a peaceful spring"

"New country rain and dew benefit the people"

"Look! Hundreds of industries rise like a forest"

"Live a life of brocade clothes and jade food, saying goodbye to poverty"

This is intentionally burying the facts and deliberately deceiving the people. In fact, there is still no place in the Northeast that can be called peaceful. Perhaps Zheng Xiaoxu, Xi Qia and others have obtained brocade clothes and jade food, but most ordinary people have lost their homes and jobs, and are still suffering from a lack of rice and clothing. How dare they talk about jade food and brocade clothes!

The twenty-eighth day of the fourth lunar month in 1934 has passed, but I don't know if this year's temple fair will be held? If it is held, will there be any new tricks? I think it won't stop, because they can take this opportunity to promote Royal Wayism again.

June Night

— Hugo, translated by Mu Mutian

In summer, at the hour when the days are done,

The plain is full of flowers, a perfumed wind;

The eye is shut, the ear is half awake,

And sleep suspends in a half-dreamed behind.

The stars are purer, the shadows seem more bland;

A gentle twilight streaks the steep dome blue;

And the pale dawn, still lingering in the land,

Looks through the heavens all the long night through.

The Third Nana

— Lingmo

Turning Nana into the Camille is not a very clumsy technique. Nana is indeed evolved from the Camille. It is not impossible to call Nana the second Marguerite, or to call Marguerite the first Nana. They are both women who have been trampled upon. Marguerite does not understand the men who trample on her any less than Nana does. But Marguerite still dreams of pure love丨丨 In fact, Nana also has some of this丨丨 sublime sacrifice, so she suffered double trampling. No matter how respectful and loving she is to Mr. Grand Lieu until death, the trampling she receives from people like Grand Lieu is no less than that from people she hates.

Nana no longer believes in the sanctity of noble people. Although she also gets the love of pure youth, she is only afraid that this is a sin, and does not feel that this can lead to an ideal. She escapes from this trampling, and also has a more courageous way to deal with another kind of trampling. She is trampled by men, but at the same time she also tramples on men. The ravages of the flesh and money are only details. Her great success is to make people know that in addition to the so-called soulless women, there are also equally soulless men.

I dare not say what Zola meant by calling Nana a poisonous fungus. Of course, I don’t even know if he was thinking about whether to put it out, and how to put it out. Although most writers are prophets, Zola is still far from another kind of society after all. We are not much different from the early nineteenth century. Most people still want to re-entangle Nana in Marguerite's dream, so that Nana will be saved, and society will be saved. The Nana in the movie was produced under this psychology.

However, in today's society, there are also women like Duncan. People who ignore Duncan's art probably won't think of Duncan as much higher than Nana. The men in Duncan's life are actually not as cute as Duncan wrote. Gordon Craig wanting her to sharpen pencils for him at home is not an unusual man. As for that rich man, Rohon Lee, in any case, he is always an uncomfortable character. Perhaps Duncan is too great, perhaps she is too weak, she has never controlled men like Nana.

But in today's society, only Nana can avoid suffering too much. In a society where there are still many men who trample on women, there will eventually be just as many women who trample on men. This woman will not be a simple Nana, but will be a Nana with Duncan's ideals, the third Nana, and she may not still be a poisonous fungus.

Miscellaneous Notes on Reading "A Hundred Schools of Novels of the Huangming Dynasty" (Continued)

— Shu

(IX) In "Eryou Weitan," there is another story that is also very good, and it is also recorded here. The text says: "My nature is not tolerant of wearing a hat and belt, especially in the hot months. Yuzhang likes to be hot early, and this year is even worse. On the seventeenth day of the third spring month, I entertained guests at the Tengwang Pavilion. The sun came out like fire, and sweat followed in succession. My head was sweating so much that I almost didn't know how to go home, and I shouted madly. My wife prepared a bath for me, so I went to it with my head bare and my body naked. At that time, the West Mountain was full of clouds and fog, and the new tea had just arrived, which Zhang Youbo happened to leave as a gift. The tea color was white and large, with a bean fragrance, almost comparable to Tiger Hill. I was bathing out at that time, sitting naked under the bright moon, and hurriedly ordered the servant girl to fetch new water to cook and taste it. I felt the water entering my throat, and a wind blew through both armpits. I thought that this realm was not found in the officialdom. Mr. Linquan Cai was old and addicted to tea, even more than I was. At that time, he had already gone to bed, and it was impossible to call him to drink it together. I cooked it again in the morning and left it for him, but it was already a second meaning. Recalling the taste of last night, I wrote a letter to give to Sheng Sheng." What is called "clear, elegant and enduring," this article can be said to have it.

(X) In Hu Yinglin's "Remaining Words of Jia Yi," there are also several readable stories, such as "Wang Taipu" and other articles. In terms of expressing emotions, there is only "Li Weiyin." He said: "Li Weiyin Taibao only changed the cold and heat once or twice, and then he was not good at walking. He staggered out of the guest room, the road was very diligent, to the point that tears fell and he couldn't stop. Because he remembered when he ran horses in Changgan and jumped over streams in Zhongling, how agile he was? And once he was weakened, he knew how much life's prosperity could be relied on. I couldn't help but look in the mirror and sigh for the silk. "There are many short lyrical articles of this kind in books such as "Baoyan Tang Secret Collection," but there are not many in "A Hundred Schools of Novels," which is thought to have been deleted by the editor.

The above is a postscript to ten anecdotes, miscellaneous notes when reading "A Hundred Schools of Novels of the Huangming Dynasty." When I finished reading it, Lingfeng used the raw draft of "Long Live" and took the cold, sarcastic and satirical parts to make an article "Jokes of the Ming Dynasty" for him. Recently, after rereading the entire book, I still cannot stop writing, so I made this article again. Among the hundred schools of novels, the systematic and excellent ones that I like to read are Gu Yuanqing's "Yunlin Yishi," which writes about the life of Ni Yunlin, Zhang Hongpan's "Xizhou Hepu," which recalls the past events of deceased friends, Fei Yuanlu's "Xiaocai Qingke," which writes about local scenery and life, and Lu Can's "Dongxiao Ji," which records ghosts and romantic encounters, but the length is longer, so only included in the personal secrets. As for matters involving literary nets and banned books, they should be recorded separately.

Fire Disaster (8)

— Fei Er

That afternoon, I obtained some travel expenses from my uncle, Mr. Zhang, and friends. Against my will, I boarded a crowded car and returned to Medan. At that time, I only had the clothes on my back, and everything else was buried in the fire. Alas, it is so heartbreaking that those precious documents and photos that I had collected with so much effort, time, and money were completely lost!

In Medan, I composed my disillusioned heart and tired body. I purchased new travel necessities and borrowed some money from friends before returning to my country in disappointment. After returning home, I reported the detailed circumstances to the principal of a certain school and the editor of a bookstore. Besides expressing their condolences, they also comforted me with a few words.

A month after returning home, I received a letter from Mr. Zhang, postmarked from Singapore: "In the disaster of January 10th, you unfortunately suffered the same calamity. How unfortunate is your fate! Thinking of the fierceness of the wind and the intensity of the fire that night, I still feel palpitations! My father's fifty years of arduous efforts and foundation were destroyed in one day. How painful! Fortunately, Mr. Xu Youwen, the owner of Guanglong Company, is my father's sworn brother. Although he is not very familiar with the ways of the world and is lightly lectured, he is still trying every possible means to rebuild the business in the future, and will certainly not be harmed by others' schemes. However, since the foundation has been ruined, it is now completely different from the past. I heard that although the fire originated in our store, the source of the fire actually belongs to your uncle... There is quite a bit of gossip among the overseas Chinese community, and the resident government is also sending out detectives to investigate, fearing that the truth will come to light soon."

Although this letter caused some anxiety in my heart for a while, I gradually forgot about it because of the struggle for life. Suddenly, eight months later, I received another letter from my uncle from his original home in Guangdong, with a remittance enclosed. The letter said: "At the beginning of the year, my nephew went south and stayed in my store for only one day. How unfortunate that his fate was so difficult that he shared the disaster of the fire god. I deeply sigh for my nephew! Afterwards, I was subjected to slander and accusations, and many people in the port placed the blame for the fire on me. What is even worse is that Guanglong Company in Singapore, because Fuhua Company in this port owed them a lot of money and they could not recover it, did not consider that the fire originated from Fuhua and actually instigated a young man with the surname Zhang to collude with ignorant people in the overseas Chinese community to accuse me of deliberately setting the fire because of business failure, in order to alleviate the economic crisis and attempt to receive insurance money. My nephew, how can I, who has lived an honest life, endure this unjust grievance? Therefore, I hired a lawyer to write a defense. At this time, the insurance company also sent detectives to investigate and spy on various parties. Fortunately, a few enlightened and fair people in the port helped me, proving that my accounts were clear and that my assets exceeded my debts, so there was no need for such a base and vicious plan. The Kapitan (Note 14) is the leader of our overseas Chinese and has a duty to speak out. He is an enlightened person, so he strongly defended my innocence. Thus, the half-year-long unjust case was finally cleared, and I have now received the insurance money. After using eighty thousand to repay debts and ten thousand for litigation costs, there is still ten thousand shields of silver left. Thinking that I have spent my life in a foreign country and endured many hardships, I am now old and should retire to my hometown, relying on a small piece of land to end my days. I heard that your suitcase contained many documents and images, which could not be rescued at that time, which is regrettable! I am now sending a remittance of one thousand yuan, hoping you can collect it from the Maritime Bank to compensate for your loss. Then the previous matter is only worth a smile, and you can avoid any loss!"

This letter made me feel dejected for several days! The one thousand yuan could temporarily alleviate my urgent needs, but how could the effort or time spent on those precious documents and photos be compensated by one thousand yuan? Moreover, fortunately, I was able to recover some of my losses, but what about those propertyless shop employees and workers who depended on that place for a living; or those overseas Chinese who had a little property but lost their settlement and the basis of their lives inherited from their ancestors? What other way could they continue to live besides suffering an unjust disaster?

(Note 14) In addition to using tribal chiefs to help them manage the indigenous people, the colonial government also set up several official titles such as "Ma Yao" and "Kapitan" in the Chinese community to help them manage the Chinese. The authority of the Kapitan is not very clear in law; naturally, they have no power in politics, but they are very useful in managing the tax collection and disputes of the overseas Chinese. (The End)

Now, because of my editorial responsibility, I am afraid of causing misunderstandings from all parties, so I have to notify Mr. and ask Mr. to publish this letter in the Free Talk section."

While the editor was trying to investigate the truth of the matter, someone had already publicly exposed it in another newspaper. Therefore, I have no choice but to publish Mr. Liu Bing's letter as follows. According to the custom of this newspaper, the manuscript fee is cancelled.

Shenbao Local Supplement

Banning Women's Strange and Unusual Clothing

— Chen

Indeed, in recent years, women's clothing has become so bizarre and unusual that it is almost indescribable. Sometimes shoulders are fully exposed, and suddenly powdered legs are completely revealed, reaching the height of fashionable modernity. Fashion entrepreneurs and new clothing companies advocate and call for it, and countless young ladies and grandmothers follow and compete, singing in harmony, forming a magnificent spectacle of colorful hues! Since women's clothing has become a fashionable pursuit of "utmost beauty and meticulous study," it is bound to violate the main purpose of "clothing to protect the body" and degenerate into a nauseating phenomenon. The so-called "showing off strangeness and competing in skill not only harms health but also damages public morals" is precisely the case.

Originally, this trend grew as society approached twilight, and people sought carnal pleasure to forget reality. It was by no means caused by moralists lamenting "the decline of public morals and the loss of ancient values." Therefore, its elimination is no longer a local "public morals" matter but has become a social problem closely related to it. We see that although the New Life Movement, which advocates frugality, is sweeping the country, it has not affected the love of beauty in wives and concubines. The fact that strange and unusual clothing is still prevalent is a clear example. However, the current government is also paying attention to the damage to public morals and health caused by strange and unusual clothing and is taking measures to ban it. This is of greater merit than the irregular destruction groups of modernity and is a head-on blow to fashionable women at this moment.

According to reports, the Jiangxi Provincial Government, upon receiving an order from Chairman Chiang, has already formulated measures to ban strange and unusual clothing, ordering the Provincial Public Security Bureau and relevant departments to be informed. The longest cheongsam must be one inch from the back of the foot, the highest collar must be one and a half inches from the jawbone, the shortest sleeve length must be even with the elbow joint, and the slit must not be more than three inches above the knee, etc. It will first be implemented among female civil servants, female students, and family members of civil servants, and then promoted to women from other regions and fields. Women who do not comply with these measures in their clothing will be subject to intervention by patrol officers. If there is resistance, they may be detained and punished. Similarly, such a ban was seen in the Lu Province authorities not long ago. It is said that Guangxi is even more swift and resolute, with female students not only advocating simplicity but also considering it a virtue to become nurses and servants.

Let those aesthetician gentlemen praise women's clothing of "showing off strangeness and competing in skill" as a manifestation of social civilization. If we examine the social implications it represents more carefully, the conclusion cannot but be "when a state is about to perish, there must be monsters." Is it simply that women subjectively want to be fashionable and modern? It is certainly not necessarily so. China is currently a society of national economic bankruptcy, upheaval, and unrest. In the process of this bankruptcy and unrest, it is divided into two extremely disparate classes. The upper class leads a life of indulgence, luxury, and licentiousness. Spending hundreds of foreign dollars on a pair of wedding leather shoes and using several buckets of milk for a bath is not uncommon. As for the countless women who have fallen into the hunger groups, on the one hand, extreme poverty reduces the number of men who can "establish a family and a career," and the female element is excessive. On the other hand, these many women feel the pressure of the economy and are brought to the human flesh market to satisfy the lusts of the general "sex maniacs." The former strives to win the exclusive favor of the "three big and two small," and the latter dresses up the goods to attract customers widely. Thus, every muscle and every appearance is made to the utmost. This is why women's strange and unusual clothing has become popular.

Therefore, to ban and eliminate women's strange and unusual clothing, the first thing to do is to fundamentally eliminate the psychology of women using this to please and cater to men. To remove this psychology of women, we must first abolish the social genes that cause women to indulge in lust, leave pleasure, and be sold as flesh.

Seeing Off

— Especially

Dark night sky, dark metropolis, dark faces of people... In short, everything is dark, everything is surrounded by darkness.

In this dark environment, Tie was unfortunately sent to an unknown hospital. Suffering, naturally, was unavoidable. When he was in anguish, depressed, and tormented, making it difficult for him to endure, he became aware. He had complained about the unreasonableness of all this established form, and he had vowed to remove the current obstructing demon. His illness gradually improved, and no matter what, he would not forget the deeply imprinted shadow. At this point, he had prepared to dig and cultivate this difficult work. However, countless demonic hands were pulling at him, threatening him. As a result, he could not but retreat under double duress.

A few days later, he gave me this letter!

! ... Brother was misled by female lust, his reputation was ruined. I want to commit suicide, but I am afraid that the world will despise me. To avenge and雪恨, I do not have the ability. Staying here for a long time, my eyes and spirit are hurt, so it is better to leave this source of sin. ... I plan to take a boat back to my hometown tomorrow night, because my hometown, although bankrupt, has its own natural 清趣, unlike the city, which specializes in showing off 声色...

In order to have a last word at the farewell, I ran to his house very early after finishing work. Pushing open the door, the order in the room was very chaotic. Tie's face was covered with a very forced joy. Facing me, he did not say anything, only smiled bitterly, as if wanting people to understand the meaning of it.

At the beginning of summer, although the hours of daylight have increased, in the blink of an eye, the lights were on again. I do not know why, but today I only feel emptiness in my heart. The electric lights are also particularly dim, and everywhere shows a kind of desolation.

Dinner was set on the six-immortal table. This time, I added a few dishes with the remaining meal tickets and bought some yellow wine to extinguish the inner gloom. We sat opposite each other, the air was very solemn, solemn, almost frighteningly solemn. The heart sound was playing clearly. The wine was slowly reduced, and it was dry. There was no mirror, but I only felt a little fever on my face, and my eyes were hot.

The clock struck ten times. The Zhabei after the war was as silent as death. The night sky was so dark, without stars, without moonlight, without flowing clouds. Two rickshaws were running on the bumpy stone road. Beside the road, there were no tall buildings or mansions. Those low ones were a group of thatched sheds with a musty smell! There was no need to write down the road name, and there was no need to know the direction. Everything was left to him to run.

After turning several bays, we pulled up to a pier. Hey, that's right, the lights on the pier are quite bright! On the left, a boat was moored, and several people were climbing up one after another. The river is so black, and the sound of the paddles is so crisp!

I bought a berth, spread out the luggage, and sat down. There was nothing to say. Yes, 生離和死别 are the most painful in life, let alone people who have been greatly stimulated and have another kind of mood? I wanted to persuade him, and I wanted to comfort him, but how to open my mouth? A belly full of words was blocked in the throat, and I could not utter a single sound.

The night was deeper, and the wind from the river blew in from the window, making people feel a little chilly. Looking at the time, it was almost twelve o'clock.

! Goodbye, I wish you well on this trip, and I will have news from you often!

My voice was a little trembling, and his eyes were also a little red.

For some reason, the two of us held hands, and a burst of cold air was transmitted all the way from the palm of his hand.

No stars, no flowing clouds, no moonlight. Everything. Is covered by darkness

Long Journey

— A Ping

The sun has fallen into the mountain hollow on the opposite side. A heavily laden two-wheeled cart is advancing on the long journey, four in front and two in the back. They started their journey when they rose out of the sun. Now, their shadows are drawn long in the opposite direction.

Except for a quick lunch at noon, they have not rested, pushing this heavily laden two-wheeled cart step by step from this town to that town. And year after year, they travel back and forth on this long journey, without a day of rest, just like they cannot not eat for a day.

The sun has set in its final moment, with only a few colorful clouds struggling at the end. The day is over. After crossing the small bridge in front, you can see the teahouse sign in this town.

The older one in front waved his hand. The other five, as if adding greater strength to their arms tanned by the sun, with a "yo" and an "yi," six bodies struggled to form an acute angle with the ground. The blood vessels on their calves burst out like earthworms. The cart was finally dragged onto the bridge deck. They gasped slightly and rudely wiped the sweat from their foreheads with the back of their hands. The ropes were unloaded from their shoulders, and the six bodies leaned back again, slowly lowering the vehicle off the bridge deck.

Following the sloping slide, they ran easily for a while. The tea house owner's laughing posture was already standing in front of them. They had handed over their responsibilities for the day. After the vehicles stopped, six people jumped under the tea shed, and the waiter had already brought three basins of water for washing their faces. Each person stripped off his upper body and washed, rudely gathered around the table, and drank the lukewarm tea, truly like oxen drinking water, a large tank of tea evenly distributed into the stomachs of six travelers.

This is the happiest time of their day. The evening curtain has already covered them, and the night breeze is blowing on his strong body, as comfortable as being stroked by a lover. Some also slightly close their eyelids, their heads leaning against the pillar of the tea shed, fantasizing about their hometown. This must be the time when the children are catching cicadas.

The tea house owner, always laughing, seeing that they were resting comfortably, bit his dry tobacco pipe and ran over, laughing loudly first:

"Guys, what are you eating?"

Although this is a daily routine, and has been for years, eating some large buns and beef, the boss seems to be relieved only after asking; and without telling jokes, if you want to change the taste, this tea house cum restaurant owner simply cannot make a second dish.

"Come on, stop nagging!"

The older one shouted impatiently. Among them, they do not know what politeness is. They say what they want to say in their hearts straightforwardly, so the boss, after hearing this, still laughs and hurries to the stove.

After filling their bellies, they treasuredly took out cigarettes from their pockets to smoke. Some smoked only a small stub before quickly extinguishing it and hiding it back in its place. At this time, they were all in high spirits. The boss also joined their group, chatting and laughing wildly, talking about women, and they made even more grotesque gestures. They had forgotten the hardships of the long journey and completely immersed themselves in the embrace of the night.

However, "Brothers, let's sleep!" the older one ordered. He pointed to the vehicle under the moonlight, saying that they had to unload the cargo before dawn tomorrow to make it back to town in time.

The tea tables and benches inside the tea shed were all their temporary sleeping beds. Without mattresses or quilts, they slept so casually, completing their responsibility as human beings for the day.

Mother and Son

— Wei Huan

Six-year-old Bao'er, lively and clever, was doted on by everyone who saw him. He had a pair of big, round eyes and a nimble little mouth.

"Mom... Mom..." he used this tone to call his mother when nothing was happening.

His mother was doing her needlework when she heard the call, and subconsciously glanced at him. In the past, she would have quickly looked away and continued sewing the clothes she hadn't finished. But today was a little different, as if she had seen a secret.

"Bao'er!" Come here. Who caused this blood on your head? Tell me quickly! She stared at Bao'er with a stern look.

"Mom, it doesn't hurt," he said, looking at his mother as if asking for forgiveness.

He often saw his mother get angry, so he would alertly hide in the corner of the wall, ready to run away quickly if she came to hit him.

"Are you still not going to tell me?" Her voice was obviously angry. She threw down the clothes in her lap, quickly picked him up, and gently wiped away the blood. The blood hadn't dried yet, so she pressed incense ash on it.

"Bao'er, you have no father or siblings. What a hard life! In the future, don't go out to play with A He anymore. Just play here nicely, Bao'er, do you understand?" Her voice trembled as she spoke.

Seeing that his mother's anger had subsided, A Bao quickly slipped away.

Outside the gate was the home of his friend, A He, who was two years older than him and had a fierce face. The gentle A Bao was often beaten by him. He went out the gate and seemed to have forgotten what his mother had told him. He quietly stood in the corner of the wall, peeking at them eating cherries. He watched them eat with relish, the cherries red and sweet, stuffing them into their mouths one by one. Saliva dripped constantly into his stomach, and even flowed out of his lips. He imagined that his index finger tasted like their cherries. His black, shiny eyes rolled like a hawk's as he thought of seizing a handful when they weren't paying attention to see what they tasted like. He tiptoed to the table and gently grabbed three cherries, but A He's sister saw him.

"Brother, A Bao is stealing our cherries!" They eagerly chased after him and finally caught him.

At this time, A Bao still refused to let go of the cherries in his hand, and their white hands pinched his small hand until it was red. "You stole our things, and you still won't let go?" The siblings shouted. He refused, they persisted, and a chaotic fight broke out. A Bao was outnumbered and cried loudly, and at the same time, he was hit on the head again.

His mother ran out at the sound of his crying, took A Bao's hand, and led him home.

"Bao'er, who bullied you again?"

A Bao cried and rubbed his eyes.

"Don't cry. Your father will bring you something even better to eat tomorrow," she said gently, stroking the bump on his head.

She lowered her head and sewed tirelessly. Two years passed quietly like her thread and needle. But she didn't feel lonely. All her future hopes were pinned on A Bao. No matter how extremely annoyed she was, she only had to look at A Bao, and all her troubles would disappear. Just like people in the darkness eagerly awaiting the coming of light.

The round moon poured down like mercury on the ground, grass, roofs, and all the scenery, turning it into a beautiful and serene village. A gentle breeze carried a warm breath, caressing the mother and son. A Bao stayed by his mother's side, constantly looking at her face. "Mom, what happened to the story you told yesterday? Did his father come back? Please tell it to me again!" A Bao used his clever eyes to ask his mother to continue the story.

"Bao'er, you like to listen? Then I'll continue... At that time, she wrote letters several times to urge him to return. One afternoon, he really came back... He was very thin and pitiful. Bao'er... He was suffering from terrible consumption, and there wasn't enough money to treat him. He hadn't been home for even a month before he abandoned his mother and son and went far away, perhaps never to return. He left behind a four-year-old child and a young woman. In this world, a son without a father and a woman without a husband never received people's sympathy... Their life afterwards was undoubtedly very difficult. Her child, it is said, is now six years old. His mother loves him very much, and his name is Bao'er." As she spoke, A Bao fell fast asleep on her lap. Tears fell from her eyes like broken beads, shimmering in the bright moonlight.

Master Yan Ganyuan of Wanzhao Lou is renowned at home and abroad for his painting skills, especially his finger painting and calligraphy. An exhibition is scheduled to be held at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai on June 15th, 16th, and 17th. The following is his work.

Nudity Movement

— Ya Fei

The body is originally the model of a spiritual animal, and humans are of course the same. The difference between male and female is a physiological difference with different forms and personalities. The difference in physiological relations between men and women also leads to many divisions and miracles. In fact, the five senses and limbs are not much different between people, and life is the same.

Those who create theories of beauty and ugliness in the world often use external appearance as the standard. Therefore, for thousands of years, Song Yu, Pan An, Xi Shi, and Wang Qiang have been envied by the world, while Meng Yang, Momo and the like have been abandoned by everyone.

In the past, when Xi Shi frowned due to heart disease, everyone thought it was beautiful. Therefore, later beauties always had to have a bit of sickness. However, in modern times, when European styles swept across China, those weak and sickly beauties jumped up and transformed into female heroes with strong bodies, nakedly offering the beauty of their flesh to the people. As a result, on the streets and markets, we often see modern misses with curves fully exposed, jade legs looming, and bare breasts and arms swaggering through the city, attracting a group of lustful men who are truly drooling. Recently, some people feel that baring their chests and arms is not enough, and they have boldly advocated the nudity movement, determined to completely expose the male and female secrets that people have avoided talking about in ancient and modern times. For several years, the nudity movement has been rampant, but unfortunately it has been banned by the authorities, so it cannot spread quickly and become popular everywhere. The general naked comrades feel very disappointed!

According to this trend, it first started in Germany, followed by the United States. In our country, Hankou, several years ago, there was also a rumor about this, but after a while, it was banned by the authorities. Recently, Hong Kong, in the place called Xiangfen Liao, the holy land of nudity, has a "Nudity Sports Meeting". The chairman is a Westerner named Dalian, and there are quite a few comrades in the meeting. However, no women have joined yet, which is a bit of a pity! But they have a positive approach, that is, every member must bring a woman to participate. Recently, the weather has been getting hotter, and the muggy heat is approaching. Therefore, the naked movement has also become active in a timely manner. It is said that the association has also prepared to operate in various provinces and ports. According to Dalian's expression to others, he seems to have some confidence in this. This matter seems credible, because we saw in the Japanese newspaper in Shanghai that "The hot summer is approaching, and the nudity movement is rampant in Shanghai. It is said that a branch has been established in the Hongkou area, and it is said that the concession will never allow it to stand..." That's right, we seem to vaguely remember in our vague minds that this happened around this time last year. But unfortunately (?), the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce learned of this news and immediately sent a letter to the concession authorities to ban it. As a result, this sensational, highly anticipated nudity movement did not appear in Shanghai after all, and we can only lament our shallow eye blessings! If this year's action is tolerated by the concession authorities, then it seems that those half-covered and half-hidden things can disappear, and we can simply play a completely naked and unclothed beauty of nudity. Anyway, everyone has a body, so what mystery is there? Returning to the original state and returning to natural life, wouldn't that be great?

The advocates say: "The nudity movement is not a shameful thing. It has a great relationship with mankind, because sunbathing, air bathing, and water bathing in nature can make people's bodies strong and clean. Moreover, we have a clear conscience and a clean body. We frankly meet you and me. In fact, we cannot say that it is a shameful thing. Humans are not shameless, but stealing, adultery, and being a prostitute, doing things secretly, this is shameful! In China for thousands of years, the relationship between men and women has been seen as too mysterious, so there is such a legacy!..." According to their expression, it is worthy of being justified and has a bright attitude. It is just like a certain doctor who advocated "sexology" a few years ago, which is really wonderful and bold. Whether this fact can be realized, we may as well wait and see.

Selling

— Fei

In order to continue life, we have to find ways to maintain life. However, in order to maintain life, everything has to be sold. Selling personality, selling conscience, selling the body, selling wives and children, selling smiles, selling blood, selling labor, selling brainpower, selling... Good! Sell it, sell it as much as possible! Anyway, in the real world, everything has to be sold, and everything has to be sold cheaply!

However, I have no conscience to sell, and personality is also a worthless thing. The body is a stinky skin, and wives and children are even more unnecessary to say, of course no one wants them. Smiles are bitter smiles, full of hot tears, who would welcome them? As for blood, I am also a person suffering from anemia, where is there blood to sell, so my only sales target is labor and brainpower; although, I also know that selling labor and brainpower is the most painful thing and you cannot get a reasonable price, but you can't do it without selling. And, sometimes, maybe even labor and brainpower have not been accepted by the master! I want to not sell! However, the heavy burden of life is tightly pressed on my chest; that would make me involuntarily sell it. However, as a result of the sale, life is still not continued.

Speaking of my current life, it is truly a non-human life, only in subjugation and under oppression all day long. A full seventeen hours of work a day, and the reward is only a few cents, the food, housing, and clothing are not as good as those labor saints. What's more, in addition to selling labor, I have to sell brainpower! Who knows the pain of selling brainpower, but even the freedom to sell brainpower has been almost deprived of me.

Humans need life to maintain life, but where can life be found? In such a society, in such a world, everywhere they are shouting "recession", and various industries are overstaffed. Finding a place to eat is as difficult as climbing to the sky. However, the world is full of contradictions, and society is developing in a deformed way. In this unbalanced state, those who advance excessively advance, and those who decline successively decline. Those who sell brainpower and labor are always not full, on the contrary, those who sit still all day long eat until their stomachs are bulging. On the one hand, money and women are dancing in their arms, while we only have brainpower and sweat blood spurting out, constantly spurting out! Alas! What kind of society is this?

The Literary Arena and the Business Arena

— Qi Sheng

The literary arena was originally a place for people who wielded pens to make friends through writing. However, since a group of merchant writers with abacuses swaggered in, the literary arena has become a business arena. Merchant writers do not write in order to "make friends through writing", but aim to make money. Because they aim to make money, they carelessly produce shoddy goods to deceive readers, which is called selling savage heads. And this business arena of literature is just like Qinglian Pavilion on Fourth Horse Road. There are merchants calculating and selling goods, and there are also wild chickens who sell their souls coming in with the merchants. Merchants only care about profit and do not care about personality. Sometimes it doesn't matter if they sell their personality together with their goods, as long as there is money to be made. Wild chickens flatter on the left and right and are good at pandering. They also don't care if they sell their personality together with their goods, as long as the patrons pay. Thus, the stench of copper fills the air, and they are proud and complacent. Merchant writers sell savage heads because they aim to make money. Therefore, they are all-rounders, pleasing everyone, and they also have the so-called turtle policy. The so-called turtle policy is what the "Zeng Guang" book says, "Recently learned the turtle's method, shrink your head where you should shrink your head." No matter how people scold, shrink your head and don't care, that is, the great man can bend and stretch the noble virtue of forbearance. And the wild chicken writer's wonderful trick to climb the dragon lies in praising the savage head, flattering on the left and right, and getting a few words of praise from those who really get the savage head. Flies attach to the tail of a thoroughbred horse, soaring thousands of miles, with sources on the left and right.

The transaction of selling savage heads has become a good business in the literary arena. Recently, there is a brand-new and outstanding business strategy of selling dead heads. It is said that literary people are valued after death. Therefore, merchants gather, and the prices of dead heads rise. The original products of savage heads are ultimately limited, and dead heads are even rarer. The market situation is that those with high prices are rising higher and higher, and there is no doubt that savage heads and dead heads can manipulate market prices. The business arena focuses on competition, and the literary arena is no exception. As a result of competition, wild chicken writers are promoted to savage heads by those who sell savage heads. At that time, if the market price of savage heads does not plummet, I am afraid that the old savage heads will become dead heads, and the market price of dead heads will rise even higher, which is expected.

Novel

Widow's Arch (1)

— Ling He

It was almost unheard of for a six-year-old child to be so alert as to get up quietly by himself as soon as it dawned. Naturally, this made him very excited, as long as he thought about yesterday evening, when the hired hand Grey Chicken promised to take him to the Tianban to catch crickets this morning, and he could also go to the village to play. The reason was that going to the village was very rare for him. Although his home was only four or five hundred steps away from the village, in his habit, it was almost like going to another world.

With a strange heart, he quietly groped to open every door leading to the kitchen, went out the back door and walked towards the grey house. Extreme joy leaped in his heart, and he whispered along the way:

"Brother Grey Chicken!... "

But there was no answering sound, which made him very worried. Could it be that he had already left? Sure enough, he was not seen sleeping in the grey house, and he was almost crying. He ran from the vegetable garden to the gate in a panic. The faint light was sparsely scattered on the ground. From a distance, he seemed to see a stone in front of him. He carefully hoped to step on the stone and step over it, but what he stepped on was a puddle of water. It turned out that it had rained sometime, but he remembered that there was not a drop of rain yesterday evening when the spider was busy spinning its web. Running all the way out of the gate, under the parasol tree that covered the road, he seemed to see Grey Chicken still carrying an empty basket and walking forward, with several people he recognized in front of him, all of whom were temporarily hired to help harvest the rice. So he ran over desperately, grabbed the corner of his clothes, and almost cried. He saw him stop and rub the top of the little master's head and say:

"What? Do you really want me to take you? If your mother finds out, she will scold me."

"I don't care," the little master said, "You take me."

"What does he want to do?" Another person asked. They all stopped walking.

"Last night, he told me to take him to Tianban to catch crickets."

"Catch crickets? There are plenty in your own garden, why go to the village!"

"Who knows, he just wants to go to the village with us to play."

"Hmph, this child is too pitiful. He is locked up at home all day long, and no children come to play with him. How can he not want to run outside?"

"Okay," Grey Chicken said again, "Sit in the rice basket, and I'll carry you. But if your mother scolds you later, don't blame me."

So the little master Shi Jimin happily climbed into the basket. The other basket was filled with. A large earthenware pot of tea. It was just right to carry on the shoulder, and the weight in the front and back was not much different.
